Wastewater Treatment Plant Immediate Action Projects, Package III – Appropriation and Construction Agreement
Adopt a Resolution appropriating $8,574,000 from Fund 72 Reserves to the Wastewater Treatment Plant (WWTP)
Immediate Action Projects, Package III (IAP III) project; award an agreement to Mountain Cascade, Inc. for
construction of the IAP III Project in an amount not to exceed $11,344,696; establish a contingency fund in an
amount not to exceed $2,270,000; and authorize the Public Works Director to execute the agreement in
substantially the form presented and issue change orders within the contingency amount.
CEQA: The City prepared a Final Programmatic Environmental Impact Report (Final PEIR) in accordance with the
California Environmental Quality Act (CEQA) (SCH No. 2015032006). Council on June 6, 2016, certified the PEIR. In
accordance with CEQA, the Final PEIR serves as the primary environmental compliance document for the
implementation of the Clean Water Program. The City prepared Addenda to the Final PEIR that was approved on
July 16, 2018 (Addendum 1) and April 15, 2019 (Addendum 2). This work is within the scope of the Project
evaluated in the PEIR and Addendum.

CITY OF SAN MATEO
Special Meeting Minutes
City Council
City Hall
330 W. 20th Avenue
San Mateo CA 94403
www.cityofsanmateo.org
 
May 1, 2023
City Hall Council Chambers 5:30 PM
Special Meeting
 
CALL TO ORDER at 5:30 p.m.
Roll Call
Present:
Mayor Lee, Deputy Mayor Diaz Nash, Council Members: Hedges, Loraine, and Newsom
STUDY SESSION
1.
Solid Waste Rate Setting Introduction and Overview
Jack Johnson, Waste Management Supervisor, provided a presentation on the Solid Waste Program and annual rate 
setting process. Consultants Rick Simonson and Gabe Sasser, HF&H Consultants, also presented and answered 
questions.
Council asked questions of staff.
Public Comment – Thomas Morgan would like more communication regarding large item pickups.
Council discussion ensued with consensus expressed for an interest in the combination hybrid approach, and use 
reserve funds. It was noted there was no increase in fees during Covid. An interest was expressed in exploring a 
lower rate increase due to the high inflation rate right now. 
2.
US-101/Peninsula Avenue Interchange Improvements – Project Update
Bethany Lopez, Senior Engineer, provided a presentation on the history of the interchange improvements, purpose 
for the proposal, issues with funding and outlined some options for moving forward. Options for consideration 
include 1) continue with current project; 2) add new alternatives to the project that would require less right-of-way 
acquisitions; 3) Restart the process and require less right-of-way acquisitions; and 4) Determine if congestion and 
safety concerns can be addressed in short- or long-term, without having to complete an interchange project.
Council asked questions of staff.
Public Comment – Kevin Simpson stated a desire to keep this project going; Geno Caccia, Caccia Plumbing, stated the 
need to review previous studies and do not press reset button now. Laurie Watanuki stated concern with traffic 
redirection and the impact on 3rd -4th -5th and Humboldt with the closure of Poplar. Cynthia Newton stated 
Burlingame needs to be involved and do not start over. Ashley Kline, resident of Burlingame, has children that walk to 
school and commented on the need to look at the negative impacts on her city. Lynn Lenardon stated this has been 
going on far too long, affecting property values – do not keep owners in limbo. Max Mautner is concerned with an 
arterial road to separate two of the biggest schools in our area and safety for children. David Hunt believes Poplar 
should just be closed as on-ramp and off-ramp. Henry Riggs called out collateral issues related to the project stating 
street parking is a major concern. 
Mayor Lee commented on the area having the worse rankings for safe routes to school and noted the need to give 
business owners some guidance as to where they stand on eminent domain matter. Consensus of Council is to 
7 of 1058

--- page 8 ---
City Council Special Meeting Minutes – 5/1/2023
Page 2
pursue Option #2 because of the expedited timeline, it leverages the environmental studies and analysis studies that 
have already been done, and there is funding for the design.
ADJOURNMENT –The meeting adjourned at 6:55 p.m.
APPROVED BY:                                                        
SUBMITTED BY:

Section Name: CONSENT CALENDAR
Account Number: 18-6114
File ID: 23-7393
TO:
City Council
FROM:
Drew Corbett, City Manager
PREPARED BY:
Parks and Recreation Department
MEETING DATE:
May 15, 2023 
SUBJECT:
Senior Catered Lunch Services Program – Agreement
RECOMMENDATION:
Approve an agreement with Corporate Cuisine, Inc. DBA Creekside Grill for senior catered lunch services for a three-year 
initial term, with an option to extend for two additional years, not to exceed $150,000 per fiscal year, for a total contract 
amount of up to $750,000 over five years. 
BACKGROUND:
The City of San Mateo, through its contract with Corporate Cuisine, Inc. DBA Creekside Grill (“Corporate Cuisine”) provides 
9,880 meals a year to seniors who attend the Dr. Martin Luther King Jr. Community Center and the Senior Center. 
Corporate Cuisine has been providing nutritious meals to our senior community for over ten years. In 2021, the City did a 
formal Request For Proposals (RFP) process for senior catering services. This process resulted in two bids, one from Trio 
Community Meals and the other from Corporate Cuisine. 
As a requirement of the RFP, both vendors provided sample meals and a select group of senior nutrition program 
members and Senior Citizen Commissioners were asked to partake in a blind tasting. The results of the blind taste test 
were unanimous, with all testers voting Corporate Cuisine as most presentable and appetizing. Another aspect of the RFP 
included City staff visiting the preparation locations of the vendors to view their operations. 
As a result of this RFP, it was determined that Corporate Cuisine provided the best tasting food, and their facilities 
provided a more restaurant feel versus industrialized service feel. Corporate Cuisine currently provides similar services to 
the City of Belmont and the City of Redwood City (Fair Oaks location). Overall seniors continuously provide positive 
comments regarding Corporate Cuisine’s meals. Staff researched if there were any new vendors being utilized by 
neighboring agencies providing similar services since the 2021 RFP was conducted, and it was concluded that there were 
not. 
BUDGET IMPACT:
The meal service provided at the Dr. Martin Luther King Jr. Center is subsidized through a San Mateo County Aging and

donation of $5.00 per meal. Patron cost for lunches at the Senior Center is $7.00. There are sufficient funds budgeted in 
the proposed 2023-24 budget for senior meals, and this agenda report is for contract authority only.

This is not a project subject to CEQA, because it can be seen with certainty that it will not cause a physical change in the 
environment. (Public Resources Code Section 21065.)

EXHIBIT A
SCOPE OF SERVICES
The Contractor/Caterer shall provide the following number of meals:
Monday/Wednesday/Friday – Senior Center 35 meals
Tuesday/Thursday – King Community Center 40 meals
Any revisions (reduction or increase in meal counts) will be provided to the vendor in writing at least 
one week prior to meal service date.  
Meal Component Requirements: 
Each meal must include all of the following:
-Salad
-Vegetables – ½ - 1 cup cooked or 1 cup raw leafy vegetable
-Fruit – ½ cup serving (when served as dessert)
-Vitamin A - 233 mcg/day
-Vitamin C – 25 mg/day
-Bread/Grain - 1-2 servings, at least ½ whole grain
-Fiber – 7 grams/day
-Fortified Milk – 8 oz, low fat 
-Sodium – No higher than 760mg to comply with County limit
Food Delivery
•
Food will be transported to the San Mateo Senior Center or King Community Center by 
approximately 11:30am for final preparation by caterer and/or brought to the appropriate 
temperature for serving as required by the San Mateo County Dietician and 
Environmental Health Agency. Food should arrive no earlier than 11:15am and typically 
not after 11:45am. 
•
Delivery Method: Food to be delivered in either a warming box, chilled box or in a fully 
operable catering van. Upon delivery, Contractor shall transfer food to either the steam 
table or refrigerator (whichever is appropriate.)

INSURANCE REQUIREMENTS
MINIMUM SCOPE OF INSURANCE

1. Commercial General Liability (CGL):  Insurance Services Office (ISO) Form CG 00 01 12 07 
covering CGL on an “occurrence” basis, including products-completed operations, personal & 
advertising injury, with limits no less than $2,000,000 per occurrence. If a general aggregate limit 
applies, either the general aggregate limit shall apply separately to this project/location or the 
general aggregate limit shall be twice the required occurrence limit.
2. Automobile Liability:  ISO Form Number CA 00 01 covering any auto (Code 1), or if Contractor 
has no owned autos, hired, (Code 8) and non-owned autos (Code 9), with limit no less than 
$1,000,000 per accident for bodily injury and property damage.
3. Workers’ Compensation: as required by the State of California, with Statutory Limits, and 
Employer’s Liability Insurance with limit of no less than $1,000,000 per accident for bodily injury 
or disease. 
If the contractor maintains higher limits than the minimums shown above, the City requires and shall be 
entitled to coverage for the higher limits maintained by the contractor.
Other Insurance Provisions
The insurance policies are to contain, or be endorsed to contain, the following provisions:
Additional Insured Status
The City, its elected and appointed officials, employees, and agents are to be covered as insureds on 
the auto policy for liability arising out of automobiles owned, leased, hired or borrowed by or on behalf 
of the Contractor; and on the CGL policy with respect to liability arising out of work or operations 
performed by or on behalf of the Contractor including materials, parts or equipment furnished in 
connection with such work or operations. General liability coverage can be provided in the form of an 
endorsement to the Contractor’s insurance (at least as broad as ISO Form CG 20 10, 11 85 or both CG 
20 10 and CG 20 37 forms if later revisions used).
Primary Coverage
For any claims related to this contract, the Contractor’s insurance coverage shall be primary insurance 
as respects the City, its elected and appointed officials, employees, and agents. Any insurance or self-
insurance maintained by the City, its elected and appointed officials, employees, or agents shall be 
excess of the Contractor’s insurance and shall not contribute with it.
Notice of Cancellation
Each insurance policy required above shall provide that coverage shall not be canceled, except after 
thirty (30) days’ prior written notice (10 days for non-payment) has been given to the City.

CITY OF SAN MATEO
Agenda Report
City Hall
330 W. 20th Avenue
San Mateo CA 94403
www.cityofsanmateo.org
Agenda Number:  7
Section Name: CONSENT CALENDAR
Account Number: 10-4679
File ID: 23-7290
TO:
City Council
FROM:
Drew Corbett, City Manager
PREPARED BY:
Public Works Department
MEETING DATE:
May 15, 2023 
SUBJECT:
Columbia Drive and Crystal Springs Storm Drain Improvements – Agreement
RECOMMENDATION:
Approve an agreement with Freyer & Laureta, Inc. for professional design services in the amount of $108,400; establish a 
contingency reserve of $11,000; and authorize the Public Works Director to execute the agreement in substantially the 
form presented and issue change orders within the contingency amount.
BACKGROUND:
The Columbia/Crystal Springs Storm Drain Improvements Project will divert stormwater runoff from an existing open earth 
ditch to a new stormwater collection system to be constructed within the public right-of-way along Columbia Drive, Tulane 
Road, and Crystal Springs Road. Currently, an open-earth ditch conveys stormwater from Columbia Drive within a 10-foot 
wide Public Utilities Easement (PUE) that spans between Columbia Drive and Crystal Springs Road adjacent to Tulane 
Court. The open earth ditch has eroded over time. This project will capture the runoff that enters the ditch on Columbia 
Drive and route it into a hard-piped system to Crystal Springs Road. The completion of this project will prevent further 
erosion within the PUE.
In 2018, Freyer & Laureta, Inc. (F&L) was selected to provide design engineering services through a qualifications-based
consultant selection process. F&L’s original scope of work included the following tasks: topographic survey, preparing 
CEQA documentation, permitting, preparing construction documents, and bid support. Developing a design to convey 
stormwater along Crystal Springs Road has been the biggest challenge due to the number of existing utilities within the 
roadway, which include PG&E, CalWater, Estero Municipal Improvement District (EMID), and the City’s sanitary sewer 
lines. The project is currently at 50% design.
F&L’s agreement has expired, therefore a new agreement is required to complete the design for the project. The scope of 
work in this agreement will carry over the remaining scope of the previous agreement (e.g., preparing construction 
documents and bid support) and include pothole and survey work to finalize the design alternative for the Crystal Springs 
Road portion of the project.  Based on the above, staff recommends approval of this agreement.
BUDGET IMPACT:
Sufficient funds are available in the Columbia/Crystal Springs Storm Drain Project (Project No. 468007).
ENVIRONMENTAL DETERMINATION:
This amendment is not a project subject to CEQA, because it can be seen with certainty that it will not cause a physical 
change in the environment. (Public Resources Code Section 21065.)

EXHIBIT A 
SCOPE OF SERVICES 
Task 1: Prepare Construction Documents 
F&L will prepare 50%, 90% and 100% design submittals for the proposed project. Through discussions 
with the City, the pipe alignment has been modified from the Basis of Design Report dated October 8, 
2021. The storm drain pipe along Crystal Springs Road will be above grade for the length of the 
retaining wall and a trench drain to the limit of work. F&L will engage structural engineer, Hohbach- 
Lewin, Inc. (HL), to design the pipe stand foundations for the above grade pipe for the design 
submittals. 
 
F&L will provide the City with one PDF copy for the 50% and 90% submittal for review and comment. 
We will participate in one design review workshop following both the 50% and 90% submittals. 
 
F&L will provide written response to comments provided during the 50% and 90% submittals. The 
written response to comments will include a brief description of how the City comments have been 
incorporated into the specification and/or drawings. 
 
F&L will provide a draft 100% submittal PDF copy for City final review. F&L will participate in a 
conference call with City staff to address any final minor comments on the 100% submittal to prepare 
the construction documents for bid. The final bid documents will be provided in PDF format only for 
use by the City. 
 
Task 2: Pothole and Survey 
F&L will engage potholing subconsultant, Exaro, to pothole the EMID waterline and the SFPUC 24-inch 
waterline to verify depth of existing utilities along the trench drain alignment. F&L will perform 
supplemental survey to capture additional rim and invert elevations of existing City’s infrastructure 
within Crystal Springs Road including the existing outfall location. 
 
Performance of Task 2 is contingent on the following assumptions: 
• Horizontal and vertical control will be based on existing City benchmarks. 
• The City will issue a no-cost encroachment permit for the utility potholing work. 
• Any traffic control plan required by the City will not require full-time flaggers. 
• All utility pothole repairs will be completed with hot-mix asphalt. 
 
Task 3: Bid Support 
F&L will provide bid support including the following: 
• Prepare for and attend one pre-bid meeting including preparing a meeting agenda. 
• Manage the meeting sign in sheet. 
• Prepare meeting minutes. 
• Prepare one addendum, if needed, for the Project including a draft submittal to the City.

EXHIBIT C 
INSURANCE REQUIREMENTS 
 
MINIMUM SCOPE OF INSURANCE 
Coverage shall be at least as broad as: 
1. Commercial General Liability (CGL): Insurance Services Office (ISO) Form CG 00 01 12 07 
covering CGL on an “occurrence” basis, including products-completed operations, personal & 
advertising injury, with limits no less than $2,000,000 per occurrence. If a general aggregate limit 
applies, either the general aggregate limit shall apply separately to this project/location or the 
general aggregate limit shall be twice the required occurrence limit. 
2. Automobile Liability: ISO Form Number CA 00 01 covering any auto (Code 1), or if CONSULTANT 
has no owned autos, hired, (Code 8) and non-owned autos (Code 9), with limit no less than 
$1,000,000 per accident for bodily injury and property damage. 
3. Workers’ Compensation: as required by the State of California, with Statutory Limits, and 
Employer’s Liability Insurance with limit of no less than $1,000,000 per accident for bodily injury 
or disease. 
4. Professional Liability (Errors and Omissions): Insurance appropriate to the CONSULTANT’s 
profession, with limit no less than $1,000,000 per occurrence or claim, $2,000,000 aggregate 
If the CONSULTANT maintains higher limits than the minimums shown above, the City requires and shall 
be entitled to coverage for the higher limits maintained by the CONSULTANT. 
Other Insurance Provisions 
The insurance policies are to contain, or be endorsed to contain, the following provisions: 
Additional Insured Status 
The City, its elected and appointed officials, employees, and agents are to be covered as insureds on 
the auto policy for liability arising out of automobiles owned, leased, hired or borrowed by or on behalf 
of the CONSULTANT; and on the CGL policy with respect to liability arising out of work or operations 
performed by or on behalf of the CONSULTANT including materials, parts or equipment furnished in 
connection with such work or operations. General liability coverage can be provided in the form of an 
endorsement to the CONSULTANT’s insurance (at least as broad as ISO Form CG 20 10, 11 85 or both 
CG 20 10 and CG 20 37 forms if later revisions used). 
Primary Coverage 
For any claims related to this contract, the CONSULTANT’s insurance coverage shall be primary 
insurance as respects the City, its elected and appointed officials, employees, and agents. Any 
insurance or self-insurance maintained by the City, its elected and appointed officials, employees, or 
agents shall be excess of the CONSULTANT’s insurance and shall not contribute with it. 
Notice of Cancellation 
Each insurance policy required above shall provide that coverage shall not be canceled, except after 
thirty (30) days’ prior written notice (10 days for non-payment) has been given to the City.

CONSUMER DISCLOSURE
From time to time, Carahsoft OBO City of San Mateo (we, us or Company) may be required by
law to provide to you certain written notices or disclosures. Described below are the terms and
conditions for providing to you such notices and disclosures electronically through the
DocuSign, Inc. (DocuSign) electronic signing system. Please read the information below
carefully and thoroughly, and if you can access this information electronically to your
satisfaction and agree to these terms and conditions, please confirm your agreement by clicking
the ‘I agree’ button at the bottom of this document. 
Getting paper copies
At any time, you may request from us a paper copy of any record provided or made available
electronically to you by us. You will have the ability to download and print documents we send
to you through the DocuSign system during and immediately after signing session and, if you
elect to create a DocuSign signer account, you may access them for a limited period of time
(usually 30 days) after such documents are first sent to you. After such time, if you wish for us to
send you paper copies of any such documents from our office to you, you will be charged a
$0.00 per-page fee. You may request delivery of such paper copies from us by following the
procedure described below. 
Withdrawing your consent 
If you decide to receive notices and disclosures from us electronically, you may at any time
change your mind and tell us that thereafter you want to receive required notices and disclosures
only in paper format. How you must inform us of your decision to receive future notices and
disclosure in paper format and withdraw your consent to receive notices and disclosures
electronically is described below. 
Consequences of changing your mind
If you elect to receive required notices and disclosures only in paper format, it will slow the
speed at which we can complete certain steps in transactions with you and delivering services to
you because we will need first to send the required notices or disclosures to you in paper format,
and then wait until we receive back from you your acknowledgment of your receipt of such
paper notices or disclosures. To indicate to us that you are changing your mind, you must
withdraw your consent using the DocuSign ‘Withdraw Consent’ form on the signing page of a
DocuSign envelope instead of signing it. This will indicate to us that you have withdrawn your
consent to receive required notices and disclosures electronically from us and you will no longer
be able to use the DocuSign system to receive required notices and consents electronically from
us or to sign electronically documents from us. 
All notices and disclosures will be sent to you electronically
Unless you tell us otherwise in accordance with the procedures described herein, we will provide
electronically to you through the DocuSign system all required notices, disclosures,
authorizations, acknowledgements, and other documents that are required to be provided or
made available to you during the course of our relationship with you. To reduce the chance of
you inadvertently not receiving any notice or disclosure, we prefer to provide all of the required
notices and disclosures to you by the same method and to the same address that you have given
us. Thus, you can receive all the disclosures and notices electronically or in paper format through
the paper mail delivery system. If you do not agree with this process, please let us know as
described below. Please also see the paragraph immediately above that describes the
consequences of your electing not to receive delivery of the notices and disclosures

May 15, 2023 
SUBJECT:
Wastewater Treatment Plant Immediate Action Projects, Package III – Appropriation 
and Construction Agreement
RECOMMENDATION:
Adopt a Resolution appropriating $8,574,000 from Fund 72 Reserves to the Wastewater Treatment Plant (WWTP) 
Immediate Action Projects, Package III (IAP III) project; award an agreement to Mountain Cascade, Inc. for construction of 
the IAP III Project in an amount not to exceed $11,344,696; establish a contingency fund in an amount not to exceed 
$2,270,000; and authorize the Public Works Director to execute the agreement in substantially the form presented and 
issue change orders within the contingency amount.
BACKGROUND:
The WWTP is an aging facility, and the Clean Water Program (CWP) includes a variety of capital improvement projects to 
rehabilitate and upgrade the equipment and processes. The IAP-III Project (Project) is a component of the CWP and 
includes improvements includes improvements to the WWTP’s effluent pumpstation, site waste pump station, and sludge 
heating and recirculation piping. The Project is part of the CWP’s efforts to modernize the existing WWTP and maintain 
safe and reliable operations.
The effluent pump station improvements include replacing pipes, new effluent pumps, and new flow meters. The effluent 
pump station improvements increase the reliability of the facility to discharge treated wastewater to the San Francisco 
Bay. The site waste pump station will be completely replaced as the existing equipment has diminishing reliability; a new 
piping, valve vault, and wet well will be constructed in a new location outside the solids handling building. Replacing the 
sludge heating and recirculating piping is required to support the continued anaerobic digestion of wastewater biosolids. 
These improvements are also coupled with plant wide mechanical and electrical equipment improvements.
In April 2022, the project was advertised for competitive bids, with only a single bid submitted. That bid of $19,880,000 
was 64 percent higher than the engineer’s estimate of $12,131,000. On June 20, 2022, Council adopted a Resolution to 
reject the sole bid and authorize staff to attempt to directly negotiate a contract with the bidder, which ultimately did not 
meet the City’s goals for a negotiated contract. 
Staff worked with the design engineer to revise the contract documents and update the costs to advertise the project 
again. A Notice Inviting Sealed Proposals and Bidding Documents were issued to advertise the Project on February 10, 
2023, in compliance with Municipal Code section 3.60.030. Three (3) bids were submitted and opened on April 6, 2023 
with the following results: 
Contractor
Bid Amount
Mountain Cascade
$ 11,344,696
Anvil Builders
$ 12,444 998
Monterey Mechanical
$ 20,628,000
44 of 1058

--- page 45 ---
CITY OF SAN MATEO
Mountain Cascade submitted the lowest bid of $11,344,696, which is approximately 25 percent below the engineer’s 
updated estimate of $15,248,000. Based on staff’s determination that the low bidder is responsive and responsible, staff 
recommends Council award the agreement to Mountain Cascade for an amount not to exceed $11,344,696. 
Staff recommends Council establish a construction contingency of $2,270,000. Based on staff’s prior experience with 
previous Immediate Action Projects Packages and the ongoing WWTP Upgrade and Expansion Project, the IAP-III Project 
presents a higher risk profile than other typical City construction contracts. The construction area is surrounded by 
ongoing WWTP operation and maintenance activities and the on-going construction associated with the WWTP Upgrade & 
Expansion Project. The requested contingency (20% of the construction contract) will allow staff to mitigate the risk that 
changes to the plant operations and other active construction efforts may require of this Project, as well as impacts due to 
unanticipated conditions (e.g., unanticipated underground utilities). 
BUDGET IMPACT:
In 2021, a budget of $10.252 million was established for the Project. During the design, the scope of work previously 
identified as part of another effort was added to the Project, increasing the estimated costs.  The current remaining 
budget in the WWTP IAP-III (46T010) project account is not enough to fully fund the construction agreement, contingency, 
other remaining project costs (construction management, project management, and engineering services during 
construction), and escalation. An appropriation of $8,574,000 from unassigned fund balance from the Sewer Fund 
Reserves to the WWTP IAP-III project account is required. There are sufficient funds in the Sewer Fund Reserves to fund 
the remaining costs to complete this project. 
ENVIRONMENTAL DETERMINATION:
The City prepared a Final Programmatic Environmental Impact Report (Final PEIR) in accordance with the California 
Environmental Quality Act (CEQA) (SCH No. 2015032006). Council on June 6, 2016, certified the PEIR. In accordance with 
CEQA, the Final PEIR serves as the primary environmental compliance document for the implementation of the Clean 
Water Program. The City prepared Addenda to the Final PEIR that was approved on July 16, 2018 (Addendum 1) and April 
15, 2019 (Addendum 2). This work is within the scope of the Project evaluated in the PEIR and Addendum.  
NOTICE PROVIDED
All meeting noticing requirements were met.

CITY OF SAN MATEO
RESOLUTION NO. ____ (2023)
AUTHORIZE AN APPROPRIATION OF $8,574,000 FROM SEWER FUND RESERVES TO THE 
WASTEWATER TREATMENT PLANT IMMEDIATE ACTION PROJECTS, PACKAGE III PROJECT BUDGET
WHEREAS, the Wastewater Treatment Plant (WWTP) is an aging facility, and the Clean Water 
Program (CWP) includes a variety of capital improvement projects to rehabilitate and upgrade the 
existing WWTP facilities; and
WHEREAS, WWTP Immediate Action Projects, Package III (Project) is a component of the CWP 
and includes improvements to the WWTP’s effluent pump station, site waste pump station, and plant-
wide mechanical and electrical equipment, as well as replacement of effluent flowmeters and sludge 
heating and recirculation piping; and 
WHEREAS, a Notice Inviting Sealed Proposals and Bidding Documents was issued to advertise 
the Project on February 10, 2023, in compliance with Municipal Code section 3.60.030; and
WHEREAS, three bids were received and opened on April 6, 2023 with Mountain Cascade, Inc. as 
the lowest responsive and responsible bidder, with a bid of $11,344,696; and
WHEREAS, staff recommends awarding a construction agreement to Mountain Cascade, Inc. for 
an amount not to exceed $11,344,696 and a construction contingency of $2,270,000; and
WHEREAS, the current remaining budget in the Project account is not sufficient to fully fund the 
construction agreement, contingency, and other remaining project costs (i.e., construction 
management, project management, and engineering services during construction); and
WHEREAS, an appropriation of $8,574,000 from the Sewer Fund Reserves to the WWTP 
Immediate Action Projects, Package III (46T010) project account is required to deliver this project to 
completion; and
WHEREAS, there are sufficient funds in the Sewer Fund Reserves to offset the remaining costs to 
complete this project. 
NOW, THEREFORE, THE CITY COUNCIL OF THE CITY OF SAN MATEO, CALIFORNIA, HEREBY 
RESOLVES that: 
1.
The City prepared a Final Programmatic Environmental Impact Report (Final PEIR) in 
accordance with the California Environmental Quality Act (CEQA) (SCH No. 2015032006). 
Council on June 6, 2016, certified the PEIR. In accordance with CEQA, the Final PEIR serves 
as the primary environmental compliance document for the implementation of the Clean 
Water Program. The City prepared Addenda to the Final PEIR that was approved on July 16, 
46 of 1058

--- page 47 ---
2018 (Addendum 1) and April 15, 2019 (Addendum 2). This work is within the scope of the 
Project evaluated in the PEIR and Addendum.
    
2.
An appropriation of $8,574,000 from Sewer Fund Reserves to the WWTP IAP III (46t010) 
project account is authorized.

SUBJECT:
Renewable Diesel Fuel Procurement and Delivery Services – Amendment
RECOMMENDATION:
Approve Amendment No. 4 to exercise a third, one-year extension to the agreement with Bosco Oil, Inc. dba Valley Oil 
Company for procurement and delivery of red and clear renewable diesel, and increase the amount of the extension from 
$150,000 to $300,000 for a new agreement total of $1,125,000; establish a contingency reserve in the amount of $75,000; 
and authorize the Public Works Director to execute the agreement in substantially the form presented and issue change 
orders within the contingency amount. 
BACKGROUND:
Clear renewable diesel is used to power the citywide fleet including dump trucks, street sweepers, sewer flusher trucks, 
and light-duty maintenance trucks. Red diesel is used to power off-road equipment, including the Marina Lagoon Pump 
Station and emergency generators. 
In June 2020, an agreement was awarded to Bosco Oil, Inc, dba Valley Oil Company for the procurement and delivery of 
red and clear diesel fuel. City Council approved a one-year agreement in an amount not to exceed $150,000, with four 
optional one-year extensions with the same price and terms for an estimated not to exceed amount of $750,000.  Council 
also approved the establishment of a contingency reserve in the amount of $75,000. 
In May 2021, Amendment No. 1 was signed to extend the contract using the first of four optional one-year extensions 
through June 30, 2022 in the amount of $150,000. In March 2022, Contract Change Order No. 1 was issued to add the full 
contract contingency in the amount of $75,000 due to the increase in fuel costs to provide funding through June 30, 2022. 
In June 2022, Amendment No. 2 was signed to amend Exhibit B of the agreement to add the procurement and delivery of 
clear renewable diesel fuel at the current OPIS sheet pricing quoted for Ultra Low Sulfur Diesel, and to extend the contract 
using the second of four one-year extensions through June 30, 2023. 
In November 2022, Amendment No. 3 was signed to increase the contract amount from $150,000 to $300,000 for the one-
year extension period, for a new agreement total of $975,000; and establish a new 20% contingency reserve in the amount 
of $60,000 through June 30, 2023. 
With the escalation in fuel costs and the recent usage increase due to storm related circumstances, the original five-year 
estimate in 2020 of $150,000 per year is inadequate. Staff reviewed year-to-date costs of diesel fuel for fiscal year 2022-23 
and projects a 100% annual increase in cost compared to the original estimate. 
Similar to Amendment No. 3, and based on these findings, staff recommends that City Council approve increasing the 
60 of 1058

--- page 61 ---
CITY OF SAN MATEO
amount of the third extension through June 30, 2024, from $150,000 to $300,000 for a new agreement total of 
$1,125,000, and establish a contingency reserve in the amount of $75,000.  
The term of the contract beginning in fiscal year 2020-21, including all optional one-year extensions through fiscal year 
2024-25, remains unchanged.
BUDGET IMPACT:
Sufficient funds are included in the operating budgets for the various departments that utilize diesel fuel. Fuel costs are 
charged back to departments based on actual usage and any increase will be absorbed in their operating budget. No 
supplemental budget appropriation is necessary. 
ENVIRONMENTAL DETERMINATION:
This amendment is not a project subject to CEQA, because it is an organizational or administrative activity that will not 
result in direct or indirect physical changes in the environment. (CEQA Guidelines Section 15378(b)(5).)
NOTICE PROVIDED
All meeting noticing requirements were met.

AMENDMENT NO. 4 TO THE AGREEMENT
BETWEEN THE CITY OF SAN MATEO AND
BOSCO OIL, INC. DBA VALLEY OIL COMPANY FOR 
DIESEL FUEL PROCUREMENT AND DELIVERY SERVICES
WHEREAS, the City of San Mateo (“City”), a municipal corporation of the State of California, and 
Bosco Oil, Inc. dba Valley Oil Company (“Contractor”), entered into an Agreement for red and clear 
diesel fuel procurement and delivery services (“Agreement”) on July 16, 2020; and
WHEREAS, the Agreement included an initial one-year term with four 1-year extension options 
on the same price and terms; and
WHEREAS, the City has completed the initial one-year term and executed three, 1-year 
extensions through June 30, 2024; and
WHEREAS, the annual cost of fuel has escalated such that the contracted price warrants 
amending; and
WHEREAS, the City and Contractor wish to amend the Agreement by increasing its amount and 
extending its term to include one additional year.
NOW, THEREFORE, the parties agree as follows:
1. Section 4, “Term,” is amended as follows:
The services to be performed under this Agreement shall commence on July 1, 2023 and be 
completed on June 30, 2024. By mutual agreement, the parties may extend the Agreement 
for one additional year on the same price and terms.  
2. Section 5, “Payment,” is amended as follows:
In Consideration for the full performance of the services set forth in Exhibit A, CITY agrees 
to pay CONTRACTOR a fee in an amount not to exceed $300,000 for fiscal year 2023-24, 
pursuant to rates stated in Exhibit B for the duration of this one-year extended term.
3. The remaining terms of the Agreement remain in full force and effect.

SUBJECT:
Gasoline Fuel Procurement and Delivery Services – Amendment
RECOMMENDATION:
Approve Amendment No. 4 to exercise a third, one-year extension to the agreement with Pinnacle Petroleum, Inc. for 
gasoline fuel procurement and delivery, and increase the amount of the extension from $250,000 to $500,000 for a new 
total agreement of $1,875,000; establish a contingency reserve in the amount of $100,000; and authorize the Public Works 
Director to execute the agreement in substantially the form presented and issue change orders within the contingency 
amount. 
BACKGROUND:
Gasoline fuel is used to power many vehicles and equipment in the Citywide fleet, and the City maintains a fueling station 
at the Corporation Yard.  In June 2020, an agreement was awarded to Pinnacle Petroleum, Inc. for the procurement and 
delivery of gasoline. City Council approved a one-year agreement in an amount not to exceed $250,000, with four optional 
one-year extensions with the same price and terms for an estimated not-to-exceed amount of $1,250,000.  Council also 
approved the establishment of a contingency reserve in the amount of $125,000. 
In July 2021, Amendment No. 1 was signed to extend the contract for the first of four optional one-year extensions 
through June 30, 2022 in the amount of $250,000. In April 2022, Contract Change Order No. 1 was issued to add the full 
contract contingency in the amount of $125,000 due to the increase in fuel costs to provide funding through June 30, 
2022. 
In July 2022, Amendment No. 2 was signed to extend the contract for the second of four one-year extensions through June 
30, 2023. 
In November 2022, Amendment No. 3 was signed to increase the agreement amount from $250,000 to $500,000 and 
establish a new contingency reserve in the amount of $100,000 through June 30, 2023. 
With the escalation in fuel costs and recent usage increase due to storm-related circumstances, the original five-year 
estimate in 2020 of $250,000 per year is inadequate. Staff reviewed year to date costs of gasoline for fiscal year 2022-23 
and projected a 75% annual increase in cost. 
Similar to Amendment No. 3, and based on these findings, staff recommends that City Council approve increasing the 
amount of the third extension through June 30, 2024 from $250,000 to $500,000 for a new agreement total of $1,875,000 
and establish a contingency reserve in the amount of $100,000. 
The term of the agreement beginning in fiscal year 2020-21, including all optional one-year extensions through fiscal year

2024-25, remains unchanged.
BUDGET IMPACT:

supplemental budget appropriation is necessary.

SUBJECT:
Downtown Cleaning Service – Agreement
RECOMMENDATION:
Approve an agreement for commercial district cleaning services with Frank & Grossman Landscape Contractors, Inc. for a 
term of two years, in an amount not to exceed $500,000 per year, with up to two, 1-year extensions at $500,000 per year, 
for a total not-to-exceed agreement amount of $2,000,000; and authorize the Public Works Director to execute the 
agreement in substantially the form presented and execute any amendments within the agreement amount.
BACKGROUND:
The Downtown San Mateo Commercial District (Downtown) is one of the largest on the Peninsula and includes numerous 
retail and restaurant storefronts, as well as a movie theater. Serving as a dining and recreation destination for visitors 
throughout the area, extensive cleaning is needed to keep its streets and parking garages clean and visually attractive.
Public Works manages the custodial agreement for these services and the current term expires on June 30, 2023. The 
scope of services in the current contract includes areas outside of Downtown including City Hall’s parking garage, Flores 
Apartment’s parking garage, the commercial blocks of 25th avenue, and changing out all the liners for all City trashcans 
throughout the City. To ensure consistent cleaning and outstanding customer experience, Facilities and Solid Waste 
worked together to issue a Request for Proposals (RFP) for a new contract to continue custodial services. The new contract 
also incorporates the new Kiku Crossing garage and pedestrian mall. The RFP included two parts: 
•
Part A - Deep Cleaning Services/Power Washing: Quarterly cleanings based upon need and approval of the City, 
intensive cleaning services including power washing sidewalks and garages, the pedestrian mall, and parking areas 
and stairwells. 
•
Part B - Regular Cleaning Services: Frequent, regular cleaning services including the sweeping of sidewalks and 
stairwells. 
The RFP allowed for individual vendors to submit proposals for one or both types of the scope of work. Staff received a 
total of five proposals. Three firms submitted proposals for both parts of the scope of work: Frank & Grossman Landscape 
Contractors, Inc. (Frank & Grossman), Puma Power Washing, and Aim to Please Janitorial Services. Two firms, Clark 
Services and Eco Sanitation, submitted partial scopes of work. Staff evaluated the proposals based on the firms' 
understanding of the work involved, prior experience with similar work, quality and technical ability of the proposed staff, 
and the pricing structure.  Based on a review of the proposals, staff recommends awarding an agreement to Frank & 
Grossman for all of the scope of work due to the quality of its proposal. Frank & Grossman has competitive pricing and 
maintains a significant workforce in the area to provide consistent service. They currently hold contracts to provide similar 
services with Caltrain, SamTrans, and several cities in the Bay Area. Frank & Grossman offers competitive compensation to 
its custodial staff including health and retirement benefits and complies with the City’s prevailing wage requirement. 
68 of 1058

--- page 69 ---
CITY OF SAN MATEO
Based on the above, staff requests approval of a not-to-exceed amount of $500,000 per year for the initial two-year term 
totaling $1,000,000, and if the two, 1-year extensions are exercised, a total not-to-exceed agreement amount of 
$2,000,000.  Staff has determined that the annual not-to-exceed amount of $500,000 for up to four total years, if the 
extensions are exercised, maintains consistency with the previous annual amount and provides budget for the full scope of 
work of both Part A and Part B for a total of $479,384 and approximately $20,000 of ad hoc additional cleanings. Based on 
the above, staff recommends approval of the agreement with Frank & Grossman to provide commercial district cleaning 
services.
BUDGET IMPACT:
Sufficient funds for this agreement are included in the Downtown Services budget.
ENVIRONMENTAL DETERMINATION:
This agreement is categorically exempt from CEQA as an “existing facility,” because it consists of the operation, repair, 
maintenance, permitting, leasing, licensing, or minor alteration of existing public or private structures, facilities, 
mechanical equipment, or topographical features, involving negligible or no expansion of existing or former use. (CEQA 
Guidelines Section 15301.)

A.
CITY desires certain custodial services hereinafter described.
B.
CITY desires to engage CONTRACTOR to provide these custodial services by 
reason of its qualifications and experience for performing such services and CONTRACTOR has offered 
to provide the required services on the terms and in the manner set forth herein.
NOW, THEREFORE, IT IS AGREED as follows:
SECTION 1 - SCOPE OF SERVICES
The scope of services to be performed by CONTRACTOR under this Agreement is as described in 
Exhibit A to this Agreement, which is attached and incorporated by reference.
SECTION 2 - DUTIES OF CONTRACTOR
CONTRACTOR shall be responsible for the professional quality, technical accuracy and 
coordination of all work furnished by CONTRACTOR under this Agreement.  CONTRACTOR shall, 
without additional compensation, correct or revise any errors or deficiencies in its work.
CONTRACTOR represents that it is qualified to furnish the services described under this 
Agreement.
CONTRACTOR shall be responsible for employing or engaging all persons necessary to perform 
the services of CONTRACTOR.
CONTRACTOR and his subcontractors shall comply with State’s Prevailing Wage Laws. 
CONTRACTOR agrees to comply with the City’s minimum wage ordinance as codified in 
Municipal Code Chapter 5.92, which differs from the state minimum wage and includes a Consumer 
Price Index escalator. 
CONTRACTOR or subcontractor shall not be qualified to bid on, be listed in a bid proposal, or 
engage in the performance of any contract for public work unless currently registered and qualified to 
perform public work pursuant to Section 1725.5 of the Labor Code.  For the work performed for the

City, the CONTRACTOR and his subcontractors shall pay the workers at the prevailing wage rate as

CITY shall provide pertinent information regarding its requirements for the project.

SECTION 4 - TERM
The services to be performed under this Agreement shall commence on July 1, 2023 and be 
completed on or about June 30, 2025. The CITY and CONTRACTOR, by mutual agreement, may extend 
the contract one (1) year at a time from the expiration of the initial contract term not to exceed two (2) 
one-year extensions.

request upon completion and CITY approval of the work performed.  In consideration for the full 
performance of the services set forth in Exhibit A, CITY agrees to pay CONTRACTOR an annual amount 
not to exceed $500,000, and a two-year total of $1,000,000, a fee pursuant to rates stated in Exhibit B, 
attached and incorporated by reference. If all extensions are exercised, compensation for four years of 
service will total a not to exceed amount of $2,000,000.

Without limitation to such rights or remedies as CITY shall otherwise have by law, CITY shall have 
the right to terminate this Agreement or suspend work on the Project for any reason, upon ten (10) days' 
written notice to CONTRACTOR.  CONTRACTOR agrees to cease all work under this Agreement upon 
receipt of said written notice.

this Agreement are confidential until released by CITY to the public.  CONTRACTOR shall not make any 
such documents or information available to any individual or organization not employed by

SECTION 15 - WAIVERS
The waiver by either party of any breach or violation of any term, covenant, or condition of this 
Agreement or of any provisions of any ordinance or law shall not be deemed to be a waiver of such 
term, covenant, condition, ordinance or law or of any subsequent breach or violation of the same or of 
any other term, condition, ordinance, or law.  The subsequent acceptance by either party of any fee or 
other money which may become due hereunder shall not be deemed to be a waiver of any preceding 
breach or violation by the other party of any term, covenant, or condition of this Agreement or of any 
applicable law or ordinance.
SECTION 16 - COSTS AND ATTORNEY FEES
Attorney fees in total amount not exceeding $5000, shall be recoverable as costs (by the filing 
of a cost bill) by the prevailing party in any action or actions to enforce the provisions of this 
Agreement.  The above $5000 limit is the total of attorney fees recoverable whether in the trial court, 
appellate court, or otherwise, and regardless of the number of attorneys, trials, appeals, or actions.  It 
is the intent of this provision that neither party shall have to pay the other more than $5000 for 
attorney fees arising out of an action, or actions to enforce the provisions of this Agreement.
SECTION 17 - NON-DISCRIMINATION
CONTRACTOR warrants that it is an Equal Opportunity Employer and shall comply with 
applicable regulations governing equal employment opportunity.  Neither CONTRACTOR nor any of its 
subcontractors shall discriminate in the employment of any person because of race, color, national 
origin, ancestry, physical handicap, medical condition, marital status, sex, or age, unless based upon a 
bona fide occupational qualification pursuant to the California Fair Employment and Housing Act.
SECTION 18 - MEDIATION
Should any dispute arise out of this Agreement, any party may request that it be submitted to 
mediation.  The parties shall meet in mediation within 30 days of a request.  The mediator shall be 
agreed to by the mediating parties; in the absence of an agreement, the parties shall each submit one 
name from mediators listed by either the American Arbitration Association, the State Mediation and 
Conciliation Service, or other agreed-upon service.  The mediator shall be selected by a blind draw.
The cost of mediation shall be borne equally by the parties.  Neither party shall be deemed the 
prevailing party.  No party shall be permitted to file a legal action without first meeting in mediation 
and making a good faith attempt to reach a mediated settlement.  The mediation process, once 
commenced by a meeting with the mediator, shall last until agreement is reached by the parties but 
not more than 60 days, unless the maximum time is extended by the parties.

EXHIBIT A
SCOPE OF SERVICES
1. It is the responsibility of the Contractor(s) to determine any and all taxes and include same in the bid price. 
2. The scheduling of the cleaning of garages and sidewalks will be coordinated with the City of San Mateo 
Downtown Coordinator. Work will be scheduled during periods when traffic is at a minimum, generally at night. 
Contractor(s) work may also be scheduled on weekends and holidays at the approval of the City as requested by 
the Contractor(s) demonstrating good cause. 
3. The City shall provide the following to the Contractor(s): 
• The approval of a schedule of base services proposed by the Contractor(s) 
• Necessary keys and access codes 
• Storage room 
• Parking passes 
4. To meet the City’s standards, Contractor shall schedule a walkthrough with the Downtown Coordinator 
before starting any power wash activity and develop a plan. Contractor shall schedule a walkthrough with the 
Downtown Coordinator after the completion of each power wash and get an approval that that the work is 
complete and acceptable before submitting an invoice for the work. 
5. Contractor(s) shall provide everything necessary to perform the tasks included in this agreement and the 
schedule included in– Cost Sheet. 
• Power Washing Sidewalks, Garages, and Pedestrian Mall (Bid Part A Only): To perform the deep 
cleaning tasks included in Bid Part A: Contractor shall follow Bay Area Stormwater Management 
Agencies Association (BASMAA) Certified Power/Pressure washing regulations or submit an alternative 
wastewater management strategy for City review and approval. 
• Pressure Washing (Bid Part B): Stains on sidewalks, in garages, and the area underneath trash cans 
shall be treated by a method consistent with BASMAA Certified Power/Pressure washing regulations. 
Contractor may propose an alternative treatment method for wastewater management may be 
proposed for review and approval by the City. 
• Leaf blowing/sweeping sidewalks: Work shall be coordinated with City street sweeping staff so that 
debris and litter is positioned in the gutter prior to early-morning sweeping. Some areas may require 
broom sweeping, collection of debris for disposal, and/or alternate hours due to nearby residences. 
• Sweeping garages and parking lots: Use sweeper machines and/or brooms to gather all leaves, trash, 
and debris for removal. Disposing of leaves, debris, or other waste in a storm drain is strictly prohibited. 
• Clean stairwells: Sweep, remove litter, wash with water, sanitize, and deodorize the stairwells in the 
Downtown garages. 
76 of 1058

--- page 77 ---
Contract for Services with SB854
Page 8 of 18
Rev. 9/22
• Cleaning garage elevators: Elevator floor and walls shall be swept, wiped down, mopped, and 
sanitized as    scheduled. The Contractor will operate elevators to verify operations and shall notify the 
agreed-upon City representative if operational issues are noted. Water needs to be contained and not 
enter elevator door jams/wells. 
• Empty trash cans: The public trash cans in the garages and in the Main Street Alley are not serviced by 
the City’s garbage service provider, Recology, and therefore need to be emptied by the Contractor. 
These trash cans are not included in Appendix E. 
• Replace garbage can liners: Remove and replace plastic liners inside trash cans included in scope and 
the ones in the garages and the Main Street Alley. Contractor is responsible for disposing of the old 
liners in accordance with scope item #6. Replacements will be provided at the City Corporation Yard at 
1949 Pacific Boulevard, access code will be provided. 
• Day Porter: A Day Porter shall be on-site five (5) days per week, including one (1) weekend day, during 
afternoon/evening hours for an anticipated total of forty (40) hours per week. Duties shall include litter 
removal and wipe-downs/light cleaning of garbage cans included in scope, parking machines and 
meters, bike racks, news racks, utility boxes, benches, and public tables using cleaning fluid and cloth. 
Day Porter is responsible for reporting any hot spots or action items to the City and after-hours cleaning 
crews so they can be addressed promptly. 
6. Upon occasion, the City may need to schedule additional cleanings of areas of garages, lots, streets, or 
sidewalks, etc. due to unforeseen circumstances such as storm events, special activities, or other circumstances 
that may arise over the life of the contract. The Contractor shall schedule these additional cleanings at the 
request of the Downtown Coordinator at a reasonable, convenient, and agreed upon time and at a price 
consistent with the scope of work and the cost sheet for similar regularly scheduled work. 
7. Except for the Day Porter duties, work shall be performed before 7:00 AM or after 10:00 PM as directed by 
the City of San Mateo. Most duties will be scheduled in the early morning. Regular cleaning duties included in 
Bid Part B will be scheduled on at least one weekend day (likely Saturday). When required, work may be 
scheduled on Sundays or holidays. 
8. Contractor should expect work to be scheduled early in the morning, late at night, and on at least one 
weekend day (likely Saturday). Work may also be scheduled on Sundays and holidays as needed. 
9. Contractor(s) shall report graffiti found on public property to the City’s graffiti abatement contractor through 
their mobile application. 
10. Contractor shall provide a minimum three (3) staff members working concurrently to perform the scope 
included in Bid Part B. Any deviation from these staffing levels must be approved in writing by the City. 
11. For the purpose of this Scope of Work, waste is defined as any garbage, debris, trash, dead animals, fecal 
matter, refuse, liquids, sludges, or other inherently waste-like materials managed, collected, generated, or 
disposed as part of performing services. 
77 of 1058

--- page 78 ---
Contract for Services with SB854
Page 9 of 18
Rev. 9/22
12. Contractor shall manage and dispose of all waste, whether solid or liquid, in accordance with all applicable 
laws and regulations, including City of San Mateo Municipal Code (SMMC), Garbage and Recycling, Sanitary 
Sewer Use, and Stormwater regulations. Solid wastes are to be disposed of at a designated area within the City 
Corporation Yard at 1949 Pacific Boulevard, San Mateo, CA 94403 unless otherwise agreed in writing, in 
accordance with all applicable laws and regulations, access code will be provided. 
13. Waste must not contaminate any potable water or surface water sites. Contractor shall not use drains for 
capturing wastewater. All waste from power/pressure washing shall be reclaimed and is prohibited from 
entering the storm drain system, in accordance with the relevant SMMC Chapters. Whenever possible, 
Contractor shall utilize environmentally friendly chemical products. The City will provide water for cleaning of its 
facilities. Locations of spigots (or fill locations) will be discussed and agreed upon with the Contractor(s). 
14. All surface cleaning staff shall have completed the pollution prevention training 
http://basmaa.org/Training(.) Contractor(s) shall comply with all BASMAA Best Management Practices and 
provisions of the SMMC. 
15. In the event that any area, or the portion of any area, is not cleaned to the satisfaction of City staff, 
including the Downtown Coordinator, the area shall be re-cleaned at no additional cost to the City of San 
Mateo. 
16. Any machine used in performing the work including but not limited to power washers, leaf blowers, 
sweepers, and vacuums shall be operated in accordance with SMMC Chapter 7.30 Noise Regulations.. Use of 
leaf blowers shall be in accordance with city regulations found in SMMC Chapter 10.80 Operation of Leaf 
Blowers. Contractor is responsible for reviewing the relevant chapters at 
https://law.cityofsanmateo.org/us/ca/cities/san-mateo/code. 
17. The Contractor shall perform all work in a manner to minimize disruption of normal commercial operations 
in all assigned areas. Each time work is completed, the Contractor shall clean and remove from each work area 
all waste and equipment associated with the work performed. 
18. Warning signage shall be displayed before and during cleaning in the areas being cleaned---language and 
timing of signage placement to be approved by the DC as part of the walkthrough plan. 
19. The Contractor shall perform all contracted duties or services in such a manner that does not damage 
property belonging to the City of San Mateo or other private or public property. In the event that damage does 
occur to property of the City of San Mateo or other property by reason of any cleaning services performed under 
this contract, the Contractor shall replace or repair same at no cost to the City of San Mateo. If damage caused 
by the Contractor has to be repaired or replaced by the City of San Mateo, the cost of such repairs or 
replacement shall be deducted from the monies due to the Contractor. 
20. Contractor shall submit a monthly work summary report along with each monthly invoice. Report format 
shall be agreed upon by Contractor and the City. Contractor’s invoice will not be considered complete until the 
monthly work summary report is submitted and approved by the Downtown Coordinator.

Additional Information about Downtown Parking Pedestrian Mall, Garages and Lots
Downtown Pedestrian Mall: located on two blocks of S. B St. between First Ave. and E. Third Ave. in 
Green on Downtown Map
Lot 1 - 2nd and ECR Garage: Located on the Southeast corner of 2nd Avenue at El Camino Real on the 
South side. The 2nd and ECR Garage has an elevator, two stairwells, trash cans, and a single non- public 
restroom, which is used by City staff and authorized personnel only. Four levels, 98,150 square feet.
Lot 2 - Main Street Garage: Located at 355 2nd Avenue. The Main Street Garage has an elevator, two 
stairwells, trash cans, and two non-public restrooms, which are used by City staff, commercial tenants 
of the Main Street Garage, and authorized personnel only. Five levels, 154,000 square feet.
Lot 3 - Tennis Court Garage: Located at 30 5th Avenue at Central Park under the Tennis Courts. The 
Tennis Court Garage has two stairwells, a pedestrian ramp on 5th Avenue and one into Central Park. 
One level, underground, 43,200 square feet.
Lot 4, 5, 6 - Central Garage: Located between 3rd and 4th Avenues from San Mateo Drive to B Street 
South. Address: 315 South Ellsworth Avenue. The Central Garage has an elevator, three stairwells, a 
pedestrian ramp on 4th Avenue and one-off San Mateo Drive, and trash cans. Three levels, 135,750 
square feet.
Lot 7 - Talbot’s Lot: This surface lot is located on 4th Avenue at South Railroad Avenue with 14,625 
square feet.
Lot 8 - Ravioli Lot: This surface lot is located on 5th Avenue at South Railroad Avenue with 15,750 
square feet.
Lot 9 - Transit Center Garage: Located at 385 – 1st Avenue. The Transit Center Garage has two 
elevators, three stairwells, and trash cans. Two levels, 80,000 square feet.
Lot 10 – not used.
Lot 11 - KiKu Crossing- 5th Avenue Garage: Located at 400 East Fifth Avenue. This contract is for the 
maintenance of floors 1-3 and ½ of floor 4. The structure has an elevator, two stairwells, and trash 
cans. Four levels, (one half of the fourth level is private and under a separate maintenance contract 
supplied by others.) 160,440 square feet.
Lot 12 – Flores Garden Garage: This garage of approximately 23,000 square feet is located at 2575 
Flores Street, near the 25th Avenue Commercial Area.
Lot 13 – City Hall Garage: This is the ground floor of a parking structure located between 330 W. 20th 
Avenue and 1900 O’Farrell, totaling 35,100 square feet. No services are requested for the upper deck 
or the basement level which are privately managed.

EXHIBIT C
INSURANCE REQUIREMENTS
MINIMUM SCOPE OF INSURANCE 
Coverage shall be at least as broad as:
1. Commercial General Liability (CGL):  Insurance Services Office (ISO) Form CG 00 01 12 07 
covering CGL on an “occurrence” basis, including products-completed operations, personal & 
advertising injury, with limits no less than $2,000,000 per occurrence. If a general aggregate limit 
applies, either the general aggregate limit shall apply separately to this project/location or the 
general aggregate limit shall be twice the required occurrence limit.
2. Automobile Liability:  ISO Form Number CA 00 01 covering any auto (Code 1), or if Contractor 
has no owned autos, hired, (Code 8) and non-owned autos (Code 9), with limit no less than 
$1,000,000 per accident for bodily injury and property damage.
3. Workers’ Compensation: as required by the State of California, with Statutory Limits, and 
Employer’s Liability Insurance with limit of no less than $1,000,000 per accident for bodily injury 
or disease. 
If the contractor maintains higher limits than the minimums shown above, the City requires and shall be 
entitled to coverage for the higher limits maintained by the contractor.
Other Insurance Provisions
The insurance policies are to contain, or be endorsed to contain, the following provisions:
Additional Insured Status
The City, its elected and appointed officials, employees, and agents are to be covered as insureds on 
the auto policy for liability arising out of automobiles owned, leased, hired or borrowed by or on behalf 
of the Contractor; and on the CGL policy with respect to liability arising out of work or operations 
performed by or on behalf of the Contractor including materials, parts or equipment furnished in 
connection with such work or operations. General liability coverage can be provided in the form of an 
endorsement to the Contractor’s insurance (at least as broad as ISO Form CG 20 10, 11 85 or both CG 
20 10 and CG 20 37 forms if later revisions used).
Primary Coverage
For any claims related to this contract, the Contractor’s insurance coverage shall be primary insurance 
as respects the City, its elected and appointed officials, employees, and agents. Any insurance or self-
insurance maintained by the City, its elected and appointed officials, employees, or agents shall be 
excess of the Contractor’s insurance and shall not contribute with it.
Notice of Cancellation
Each insurance policy required above shall provide that coverage shall not be canceled, except after 
thirty (30) days’ prior written notice (10 days for non-payment) has been given to the City.
Waiver of Subrogation
Contractor hereby grants to City a waiver of any right to subrogation which any insurer of said Contractor 
may acquire against the City by virtue of the payment of any loss under such insurance.  Contractor 
agrees to obtain any endorsement that may be necessary to effect this waiver of subrogation, but this 
provision applies regardless of whether or not the City has received a waiver of subrogation 
endorsement from the insurer.  
Deductibles and Self-Insured Retentions
86 of 1058

--- page 87 ---
Contract for Services with SB854
Page 18 of 18
Rev. 9/22
Any deductibles or self-insured retentions must be declared to and approved by the City. The City may 
require the Contractor to purchase coverage with a lower deductible or retention or provide proof of 
ability to pay losses and related investigations, claim administration, and defense expenses within the 
retention.  
Acceptability of Insurers
Insurance is to be placed with insurers with a current A.M. Best’s rating of no less than A:VII, unless 
otherwise acceptable to the City.
Verification of Coverage
Contractor shall furnish the City with original certificates and amendatory endorsements or copies of 
the applicable policy language effecting coverage required by this clause.  All certificates and 
endorsements are to be received and approved by the City before work commences.  However, failure 
to obtain the required documents prior to the work beginning shall not waive the Contractor’s 
obligation to provide them.  The City reserves the right to require complete, certified copies of all 
required insurance policies, including endorsements required by these specifications, at any time.

Agenda Report
City Hall

San Mateo CA 94403

Agenda Number:  12
Section Name: CONSENT CALENDAR
Account Number: 10-2312
File ID: 23-7476
TO:
City Council
FROM:
Drew Corbett, City Manager
PREPARED BY:
Human Resources Department
MEETING DATE:
May 15, 2023 
SUBJECT:
Merit Employees’ Salary Schedules – Approval
RECOMMENDATION:
Adopt a Resolution to authorize and approve the City of San Mateo Merit Employees’ current pay rates and ranges (salary 
schedule). 
BACKGROUND:
Pursuant to Municipal Code Section 4.02, the City Council provides for the compensation of all officers and employees and 
salaries shall be fixed by resolution. Title 2 of the California Code of Regulations (CCR), Section 570.5, requires the City 
Council to adopt a full salary schedule as a standalone document detailing the rates of pay for each City classification, and 
to maintain this salary schedule as a publicly available document for at least five years. The California Public Employees’ 
Retirement System (CALPERS) uses this salary schedule to determine the “compensation earnable” when calculating the 
monthly pension an individual will receive when they retire. “Compensation earnable” is defined by the Public Employees’ 
Retirement Law (PERL) Government Code Sections 20636, and 20636.1 as pay rate and special compensation as defined in 
the statutes. 
The City of San Mateo merit employees’ salary schedule is consistent with classifications and pay rates for current 
employees at this time, and no changes to the various salary ranges are proposed by the adoption of the salary schedules. 
The merit employees’ salary schedule (Attachment 1 - Exhibit A) reflects salary changes previously approved by the Council 
in resolutions. Salary schedules are available to the public on the City’s website. 
BUDGET IMPACT:
There is no fiscal impact related to the adoption of this resolution.
ENVIRONMENTAL DETERMINATION:
This action is not a project subject to CEQA, because it is an organizational or administrative activity that will not result in 
direct or indirect physical changes in the environment. (CEQA Guidelines Section 15378(b)(5).)
NOTICE PROVIDED
All meeting noticing requirements were met.
ATTACHMENTS

CITY OF SAN MATEO 
RESOLUTION NO. 
 (2023)
ADOPTING THE CITY OF SAN MATEO EMPLOYEE PAY RATES AND RANGES 
(SALARY SCHEDULE)
WHEREAS, pursuant to City Charter Section 4.02, the City Council provides for the compensation of all 
officers and employees and salaries shall be fixed by resolution; and
WHEREAS, Title 2 of the California Code of Regulations (CCR), Section 570.5, requires the City Council to 
adopt a full salary schedule, as a standalone document detailing the rates of pay for each City classification; and
WHEREAS, the City must maintain salary schedules as publicly available documents for at least five 
years; and
WHEREAS, the California Public Employees’ Retirement System (CALPERS) uses the salary schedules to 
determine “compensation earnable”; and
WHEREAS, the City of San Mateo Merit Employees’ Salary Schedule is consistent with classifications and 
pay rates for current employees at this time and no changes to the various salary ranges are proposed by the 
adoption of the salary schedules; and
WHEREAS, these salary schedules reflect salary changes previously approved by the Council in 
Resolutions; and
WHEREAS, no appropriation of additional funds is necessary;
NOW, THEREFORE, THE CITY COUNCIL OF THE CITY OF SAN MATEO, CALIFORNIA, HEREBY RESOLVES
that:
1.
The classification updates are not subject to California Environmental Quality Act (CEQA Guidelines 
Section 15061(b)(3)) because it can be seen with certainty that they will not cause a physical change 
in the environment; and
2.
The pay rates and ranges set forth in the Merit Employees’ Salary Schedule attached as Exhibit A are 
approved.

SUBJECT:

RECOMMENDATION:

Association.

an event at the San Mateo County Event Center. The City has been asked to provide a $1,250 contribution to be a 
Community Sponsor of the event. This sponsorship includes: 
•

•
Recognition on all marketing material produced for the event 
•
The City's logo on the event program and verbal recognition during the event

CITY OF SAN MATEO
CITY OF SAN MATEO
Agenda Report
City Hall
330 W. 20th Avenue
San Mateo CA 94403
www.cityofsanmateo.org
Agenda Number:  14
Section Name: OLD BUSINESS
Account Number: 10-1311
File ID: 23-7461
TO:
City Council
FROM:
Drew Corbett, City Manager
PREPARED BY:
City Manager's Office
MEETING DATE:
May 15, 2023 
SUBJECT:
Pedestrian Mall – Boundary Determination
RECOMMENDATION:
Provide direction to staff on whether to bring forward a revision to the boundaries of the pedestrian malls to reopen to 
traffic the block of B Street between First and Second Avenues and whether to allow for parklet platforms within the 
pedestrian mall.
BACKGROUND:
During the COVID-19 pandemic, the City piloted street closures on portions of B Street using temporary barricades to allow 
for outdoor dining and expanded public open space. Based on the success of the pilot, the City committed to permanently 
closing two adjacent segments of B Street between 1st and 2nd Avenues and 2nd and 3rd Avenues through the Pedestrian 
Mall Act process. The ordinance closing the street segments to establish the pedestrian malls was adopted at the October 
4, 2021 City Council meeting. Since then, staff has been working on designs for permanent barricades and improvements 
to the pedestrian mall. The design work is expected to be completed within a few months after which the City will start the 
construction bid process. The total cost of the improvements for both blocks is estimated to be roughly $1.2 million 
dollars.
The intensity of use of the two pedestrian mall blocks has been uneven ever since the streets were initially closed. Most of 
the restaurants between 2nd and 3rd Avenues have embraced the opportunity to use the outdoor space, while only two 
businesses are using the block between 1st and 2nd Avenue.  At the March 20, 2023 City Council meeting, in response to 
comments submitted by the business community, the City Council directed staff to agendize a discussion on whether to 
reopen the block between 1st and 2nd Avenue to traffic. In addition, the Council directed staff to revisit the guidelines 
related to the ability of businesses to have a parklet platform on the pedestrian mall.  It is timely to move forward with this 
discussion prior to staff issuing construction bids for the pedestrian mall improvements. In addition, staff is working on the 
artist selection process for the Racial Equity Art project that will be located within the pedestrian mall and needs guidance 
on whether one or both blocks will be available for the mural.
Business Survey
At the direction of the Council, staff developed a targeted survey to get feedback from the businesses on both blocks of 
the pedestrian mall. The survey included questions on whether they prefer their block open or closed to traffic, if they 
would prefer a seasonal closure, and if the ability to have a parklet platform would change their opinion. Additionally, the 
survey asked whether or not the events held on the street help or hurt their business. Staff was able to get a 90% response 
rate for the ground-floor businesses located between 1st and 2nd Avenue and an 80% response rate for the ground-floor 
businesses located between 2nd and 3rd Avenue. Staff included a summary of the survey results as  Attachment 1 to this 
report. The survey results are sorted by block and then also further sorted based on whether or not they are a food-
serving business.
122 of 1058

--- page 123 ---
CITY OF SAN MATEO
The majority of the businesses between 1st and 2nd Avenue would prefer that their block be reopened to vehicular traffic 
either year-round (63%) or seasonally (11%). The businesses stated that the block closure has reduced revenues, created 
logistical issues, and reduced customer satisfaction. The results differed somewhat based on the type of business.  The 
majority of the non-food businesses on the block (75%) support reopening the street to traffic whereas only 55% of the 
food/drink businesses would like to see the street reopened. Currently only two of the twelve food/drink businesses 
located on that block have outdoor dining installations but another two are considering adding them in the future.
For the block between 2nd and 3rd Avenue, less than a third (31%) of the businesses would like to see that block reopened 
to traffic and the majority of the food/drink businesses (82%) would prefer to have the street remain closed. As a result of 
these findings, staff would not recommend reopening the block between 2nd and 3rd Avenue to vehicular traffic.
Seasonal closures
Staff surveyed the businesses on both blocks to see if a seasonal-only closure would be preferred to year-round. The 
majority of the businesses did not support a seasonal closure. Only a handful of non-food businesses were interested in 
that idea. Seasonal closures would be challenging for food businesses since they do not have a place to store their 
furnishings in the off-season. As a result of this business feedback, staff does not recommend that City Council consider 
seasonal closures as an option for the pedestrian malls.
Platform considerations
Currently the businesses located on the pedestrian mall are limited to furnishings that can be removed easily for public 
events or for street maintenance needs. A key challenge with not having a platform is that the businesses are not able to 
mitigate for the slope of the street in their dining installations. If the Council were to relax this restriction, any platform 
that would be allowed would need to follow the City’s parklet guidelines and meet ADA slope standards, allow for storm 
water drainage, and would not be permitted to have roofs (although shade sails and umbrellas are allowed).
If the businesses on the pedestrian mall were allowed to have more permanent platforms it could impede the ability to 
hold street fair events on the pedestrian mall, such as the Chamber’s Reimagine San Mateo event. It may still be possible 
to allow for outdoor concert events, such as September Nights on B Street, if the businesses are willing to allow the public 
to use their outdoor dining areas during the events.
When asked in the survey if they would build a parklet platform if allowed, 45% of the food/drink businesses between 1st 
and 2nd Avenue and 73% of the food/drink businesses between 2nd and 3rd Avenue said they would. On the block 
between 1st and 2nd, 55% of the food /drink businesses would prefer the block be reopened to traffic if parklets were 
allowed. In contrast, the businesses between 2nd and 3rd overwhelmingly would prefer the street remain closed.
Impact of Events
Staff included questions in the survey to gauge the comparative impact to businesses of events held in the pedestrian mall 
versus those in Central Park. For the most part, the food/drink businesses found that events held on the pedestrian mall 
were beneficial to their businesses whereas those held in Central Park did not have any impact on them.  A portion of the 
non-food serving businesses on both blocks stated events were harmful to their business but the majority stated they had 
no impact on revenues.
Process to Reopen the Street to Traffic
The State‘s Pedestrian Mall Act outlines a detailed process in order to establish a pedestrian mall that includes the 
adoption of a Resolution of Intent, noticing all impacted property owners, holding a public hearing, and adopting the 
closure via an ordinance. The Pedestrian Mall Act does not explicitly go into details on how to reverse the decision other 
than to indicate that the City has the ability to do so. Staff would recommend that the City follow the same process for a 
potential reopening as it did for the closure. This process is expected to take several months to complete and will include 
several opportunities for comment from both the business community and the general public. 
In addition to going through the public hearing process to reopen the street, there are some minor improvements that 
123 of 1058

--- page 124 ---
CITY OF SAN MATEO
would need to be made to return the block to its former use. The traffic lanes and parking spaces would need to be 
restriped and the parking meters and related signage would need to be reinstalled. The anticipated cost of this work is 
$50,000.
Questions for City Council discussion:
•
Do you want to move forward with the process to reopen the block between 1st and 2nd Avenue to traffic?
•
Do you want to allow businesses to build parklet platforms within the pedestrian mall?
BUDGET IMPACT:
If the City were to decide to reopen the block between 1st and 2nd Avenue it will cost roughly $50,000 to implement but 
will result in a significant reduction, potentially up to $500,000, to the cost of constructing the pedestrian mall 
improvements.  The pedestrian mall improvements are included in the City’s draft Capital Improvement Project (CIP) 
proposal.
ENVIRONMENTAL DETERMINATION:
This discussion of potential revisions to the pedestrian mall boundaries is not a project subject to CEQA, because it is an 
organizational or administrative activity that will not result in direct or indirect physical changes in the environment. (CEQA 
Guidelines Section 15378(b)(5).)
NOTICE PROVIDED
All meeting noticing requirements were met.
ATTACHMENTS
Att 1 - Summary business survey results
Att 2 - Public Comment
STAFF CONTACT
Kathy Kleinbaum, Assistant City Manager
kkleinbaum@cityofsanmateo.org
