--- page 704 ---
PROPERTY OWNER APPEAL
TO:
Chistina Horrisberger, Director of Community Development Department
OWNER:
Trina Pierce
TENANTS:
Herminia Panameno, Josue N. Panameno, Patricia Panameno, and Marta Zavala
SUBJECT PREMISES: 100 N. Humboldt, San Mateo
__________________________________________________________________________
INTRODUCTION
The OWNER hereby appeals the City of San Mateo Code Enforcement’s (CE) assessment of
relocation costs – as amended (the “Assessment”).
The Assessment is the result of a “shoot first and ask questions later” process.  CE committed a
major error by completely ignoring one of the two requirements for assessing relocation costs.
Per San Mateo Municipal Code section 7.50.030, CE must establish:
(1) The existence of conditions rendering a premises uninhabitable, and
(2) Liability for the substandard conditions.
CE failed to undertake any determination of liability prior to issuing the Assessment.  In fact, 13
days elapsed between the date of CE’s inspection and its issuance of the Assessment and during
those 13 days, it never once reached out to the OWNER to get her position.  Incredulously, even
after the OWNER submitted  voluminous documentation to CE clearly establishing the
TENANTS’ liability for the substandard conditions at the Premises, CE refused to withdraw the
Assessment.  CE failed to consider any of the OWNER’s overwhelming evidence of the
TENANTS’ liability.  Its unfounded Assessment has now forced the OWNER to file this Appeal
and pay $519 to do so.  As the TENANTS are liable for the uninhabitable conditions at the
Premises and kept these conditions from the OWNER, per San Mateo Municipal Code sections
7.50.030(b)(2) and (3), they are ineligible to receive relocation costs from the OWNER.
There should have never been an assessment from which to appeal, but the OWNER has now
had to file this Appeal in order to preserve her rights.  The City should summarily grant this
Appeal, immediately withdraw the Assessment and refund the appeal fee.
The reality is that the Premises are the cherished home of the OWNER’s mother.  She leased it in
a good and habitable condition to the TENANTS.  The TENANTS had sole possession and
control of the Premises, during which time they repeatedly breached the Lease causing extensive
damages.  As a result of the TENANTS’ misconduct, in November, 2022, the OWNER exercised
her lawful right to evict TENANTS with a 60-Day Notice.  As the 60-Day deadline approached,
TENANTS requested to stay in the Premises.  When the OWNER refused, TENANTS turned to
CE to exploit the process and the OWNER and to retaliate against her.  They went into overdrive
in their destruction of the Premises, rendered it uninhabitable, then blamed the OWNER and
1
704 of 1058

--- page 705 ---
used the City to seek relocation costs.  This is a case of tenants gaming the system to extract
relocation costs and exploit a senior in the process.  Tenants are ineligible for relocation costs
because they are liable for rendering the Premises uninhabitable.  They must not benefit from
their malicious deeds.
TENANTS ARE INELIGIBLE FOR RELOCATION COSTS UNDER THE LAW
The TENANTS are ineligible for relocation costs from the OWNER because of three exceptions
to relocation costs that apply to this matter:
(1) The TENANTS caused the damages that rendered the Premises inhabitable;
(2) The TENANTS prevented the OWNER from undertaking maintenance of the Premises
and as will be proven here they not only failed to notify the OWNER of any such conditions and
provide her the opportunity to cure them, they concealed conditions from the OWNER; and
(3) There were natural disaster events that contributed to some of the conditions.
For reference, the relevant parts of San Mateo Municipal Code (the “Code”) section 7.50.030 are
provided below:
(a) A tenant household shall be eligible for relocation payments from a property owner
under this chapter if the tenant household is displaced from its dwelling or room due to
the City's code enforcement activities.
…
(b) Notwithstanding subsection (a) above, a tenant household shall not be deemed
displaced due to code enforcement activities in any of the following cases:
…
2. The property owner demonstrates to the satisfaction of the Director that the
noncomplying condition was created by the tenant household or the tenant household's
guests or invitees, and was not created by the property owner or the property owner's
agent, or that the condition giving rise to the code enforcement activities existed at the
time that the tenant household occupied the dwelling or room and that the tenant
household occupied the dwelling or room for the purpose of receiving relocation benefits;
3. The property owner demonstrates to the satisfaction of the Director that the tenant
household unreasonably prevented the property owner or the property owner's agent from
undertaking maintenance or repairs that would have prevented or rectified the
noncomplying condition;
…
2
705 of 1058

--- page 706 ---
7. The tenant household is required to vacate the dwelling or room due solely to damage
resulting from an earthquake, fire, flood, natural disaster, civil disturbance, or accident
outside the control of the property owner, if (a) the vacation is required within six months
of such event, and (b) the property owner demonstrates to the satisfaction of the Director
that such damage was not caused by the acts or the negligence of the property owner or
by a preexisting condition in the building in violation of applicable building, housing,
fire, or other health and safety codes.
(Emphasis Added).
As set forth below, the OWNER will discuss these code sections in the context of the alleged
conditions on the Premises.
BACKGROUND FACTS
THE HOME & THE LEASE: 100 N. Humboldt was built in 1940, in the redline district of San
Mateo.  The OWNER’s family bought the home in the 1950’s because it was the only area of San
Mateo in which her family could buy a home. The OWNER and her siblings grew up in this
home. It is a cherished home and is the bedrock of their generational wealth.
The OWNER leased (the “Lease”) and turned over possession of her family’s home to
TENANTS, in a condition that was clean, sanitary, in good repair, and completely free of any
infestations.  (See Exhibits A-C and D.)  In fact at that time of the Lease, the Premises passed
inspection to qualify as Section 8 housing.  In short, there was no question that the Premises
were habitable.  (See Exhibit D.)
Upon Lease execution through to January 31, 2023, TENANTS had the exclusive possession and
control of the Premises.  Landlord believed that when the tenancy ended the TENANTS would
return the Premises in the same condition as existed upon their move-in, except for normal wear
and tear.
Under the terms of the Lease and California Law TENANTS were obligated to:
●
Keep the unit in a clean and habitable condition.
●
Keep fixtures clean and sanitary.
●
Use the rental unit for living, sleeping, cooking, or dining purposes only.

maintain the Premises.  As a result, on November 17, 2022, the OWNER served TENANTS with
a 60-Day Notice to Vacate for the following breaches of the Lease:

Dear Ms. Pierce,

Patriot Environmental Laboratory Services, Inc. (Patriot) would like to present this report of a
preliminary mold investigation conducted at the above referenced residence on February 25,
2023.

It is Patriot's understanding that the client has concerns of potential mold growth within the
subject residence. The objective of this investigation was to determine if any water damage or
moisture intrusion in the residence resulted in mold amplification in affected structural
components of the building.

The investigation consisted of a visual reconnaissance of Bedroom 1, Bedroom 2, Hall Bathroom
and Upstairs Bathroom; the collection of microscopic particulate samples from building
materials within the areas suspected of being affected by the water release; and, the collection of
indoor and outdoor air samples. The sampling locations (and number of samples collected) were
determined based on visual observations of suspected mold amplification or in areas of the
residence reportedly damaged by the water release.

Ambient air samples were collected using Zefon Analytical Accessories Air-O-Cell cassettes and
high volume air samplers. Particulate samples were collected in adhesive tape and glass
microscope slides (tape-lifts). All samples collected were delivered, under chain of custody
documentation, to Patriot for identification and counting of mold spore colonies. Results of the
analysis are presented in Attachment 1.

717 of 1058


--- page 718 ---
Mold and Spore Analysis Results

Structural components in the area affected by the water damage were inspected and
representative samples were collected. It should be noted that sampling was limited to the area
suspected of being affected by the water damage and in exposed building materials and
structures.

Patriot reported the presence of mold spores in the indoor and outdoor air. The total mold spore
counts in the ambient air samples collected from Bedroom 1, Bedroom 2, Downstairs Bathroom
and Upstairs Bathroom were greater than the spore counts observed in the outdoor samples.
Attachment 1.

Analytical results reported by Patriot indicate the presence of colonies of mycelial fragments,
Aspergillus/Penicillium and Cladosporium in the particulate samples collected from the
Downstairs Bathroom (wooden window components). Attachment 1.

At the time of Patriot's inspection, Patriot observed visible mold growth in various locations
throughout the residence in the following locations: Bedroom 1 — both windows, closet walls,
closet ceilings and floor; Bedroom 2 — both windows, bedroom walls, closet walls, closet floor
and closet ceiling; Hall Bathroom — window, walls, tile grout on floors walls and shower, and
ceiling; 2F Bathroom — on the tub caulking, windows and damaged flooring. Visible water
damage was observed on the 2F Bathroom flooring. No elevated moisture readings were detected
from surfaces within the residence. Extech Temperature/Relative Humidity Meter measured an
interior air temperature of 56 F with an interior relative humidity of 50.5% within the subject

property.
Note: These results indicate that mold colonies are present at the residence.

It should be noted that in addition to the results reported above, various species of mold and
spores were detected throughout the samples collected at the residence. In addition, individual
species were identified in isolated samples. These results indicate that there is no predominant
fungal specie that dominates throughout the residence. Mold spores in trace to minor quantities
are ubiquitous and expected to be found in indoor building materials of urban properties.

Recommendations

Based on the results of this investigation and the visual reconnaissance, the following
recommendations are made (see attached drawings for general areas of remediation):

e Find and fix water and or moisture source(s). NOTE: Multiple moisture sources likely
present throughout residence due to the locations of identified mold and visible water
damage.

e Remove any water or mold damaged wood flooring in Bedroom 1 and Bedroom 2 as
well as the associated closets. After removing the wood flooring, in the affected areas, the
sub-floors should be thoroughly cleaned using wet mops utilizing a biocide agent and

718 of 1058


--- page 719 ---
vacuums utilizing HEPA filters. The objective of the cleaning is to remove excess dust,
moisture and residual mold spores.

Thoroughly scrub/clean all ceramic tiles in the Hall Bathroom using wet mops utilizing a
biocide agent and vacuums utilizing HEPA filters. The objective of the cleaning is to
remove excess dust, moisture and residual mold spores.

Remove water or mold damaged laminate flooring in the Upstairs Bathroom. After
removing the laminate flooring, in the affected areas, the sub-floors should be thoroughly
cleaned using wet mops utilizing a biocide agent and vacuums utilizing HEPA filters.
The objective of the cleaning is to remove excess dust, moisture and residual mold
spores.

Remove all cabinets in the Second Floor Bathroom and Hall Bathroom. The cabinets,
equipment, enclosures, and fixtures, once removed, should be cleaned and treated with a
biocide agent to minimize or prevent mold growth. (Note: Many equipment, enclosures,
and fixtures may not be able to be removed without damage, and some finishes cannot be
sufficiently cleaned and treated).

o Hall Bathroom (entire ceiling)

o Bedroom 2 Closet

e All wall and ceiling cavities should be thoroughly cleaned/scrubbed using wet methods
utilizing a biocide agent, and vacuums utilizing HEPA filters. The objective of the
cleaning is to remove excess dust, moisture, and residual mold spores.

e Any personal items, clothing, furniture that have visible signs of moisture, water-damage,
and mold amplification should be cleaned, treated, laundered, or dry-cleaned. Items,
which cannot be sufficiently cleaned/treated, should be properly disposed.

e Any additional materials, discovered during remediation, with visible evidence of
mold growth should be either removed or cleaned and treated with a biocide agent
to minimize or prevent mold growth. Mold affected materials may be discovered
during renovation activities conducted at the residence.

e Allremediation activities should be conducted under pneumatic isolation from the rest of
the residence. The rooms to be remediated should be enclosed to prevent dispersion of
mold spores to unaffected areas of the residence. This isolation can be accomplished by
the use of airtight enclosures in affected areas of the residence and by maintaining the
affected areas under negative air pressure in relation to the rest of the residence.
Activating any HVAC systems during any remediation activities should be avoided.

¢ Upon completion of removal and cleaning activities and prior to post-remedial activities,
HVAC ducting, registers, and returns should be cleaned. Any HVAC filters should be
replaced. The objective of the cleaning is to remove excess dust and residual mold spores.

e At the completion of removal and cleaning activities and prior to the addition of
wail/ceiling coverings and new flooring, a post-remedial investigation should be
conducted. This post-remedial investigation should include the collection of indoor and
outdoor air samples, which should be collected and analyzed to determine the presence of
residual indoor air mold contamination in the residence.

Limitations

Mold growth is known to occur in hidden areas where chronic and recurrent water releases may
occur in a structure. These areas include walls and insulating materials in bathrooms, kitchens,
laundry rooms, garages and attics under a leaking roof. The inspection reported here did not
include areas not known to have been affected by any accidental water release. In addition, no
intrusive sampling was conducted behind walls, cabinets, vanities and shower enclosures.

herefore, the potential for mold growth in these hidden areas cannot be discarded at this time.

Mold amplification is not a static situation, if elevated levels of moisture remain in the affected
areas over an extended period of time the scope of work/recommendations may increase and a

Results on this report relate only to samples submitted for analysis, they are indicative of samples taken at a given time and may not be representative of
other locales and time frames. Heavily loaded samples may have intense occlusion that may pose a bias for quantifying and identifying total spores, as
blending of spores and background/debris may occur. Results may be reported as "Present" or "Observed" if quantitative results are not requested or not
possible due to overloading or excessive ambiguity among spores and debris. A debris rating scale of 1-10 is used to indicate the amount of deposited
debris on a sample. A debris rating of 1, means that up to 10% of the field of view (FOV) area is covered by debris particles. A debris rating of 2, means
that 20% of the FOV is covered by debris. Successively a debris rating of 10 means that up to 100% of the FOV area is covered by debris particles.

The limit of detection is defined as observing 1 spore, fungal structure, hyphal fragment, or pollen grain. The analytical sensitivity for this method is
calculated as 1 observation multiplied by (((1000L / volume of air sampled (L)) x 1/m3). Percent trace read and/or sample volume drawn will
proportionately affect the reporting limit and/or analytical sensitivity. Calculations for the concentrations of spores are based on the air volume provided
by the client. Calculated data are accurate to two significant figures. Interpretation of results is left to those requesting testing. Sample condition as
received is fair unless noted otherwise. This report may not be reproduced, except in full. without the expressed written consent of Patriot Environmental
Laboratory Services, Inc (Patriot). This report may not be used to claim or imply product certification, approval, or endorsement by Patriot or any
government agency.

100 Fields of View (FOV) at 1000x magnification. The limit of detection for direct exam surface samples is qualitatively Trace, where the Analyst has
observed one (1) fungal presence in an average of 100 FOV or more. Estimated ranges. Trace: 1-100 Minor: 101-1000 Major: 1001-10,000 Abundant:
>10,001 spores. The results reported pertain only to the items submitted and may not represent the entire area from which they were taken. Results are
indicative of samples taken at a given time, and may not be representative of other locales and time frames. Bulk samples that do not have markings or
notes for specific areas to be tested will be tested at the analyst’s discretion. Where a defined unit area of analysis is requested, results will be reported in
terms of estimated spores/unit area with an analytical sensitivity of 1 spore/unit area. Interpretation of results is left to those requesting testing. Sample
condition as received is fair unless noted otherwise. This report may not be reproduced, except in full, without the expressed written consent of Patriot

04/17/2023 
FINAL NOTICE TO ABATE A PUBLIC NUISANCE 
 
You are receiving this letter as the record owner of the property located at 100 N Humboldt St. in San 
Mateo, California and it is part of the ongoing Code Enforcement Case. On 02/01/2023 (copy 
attached), we notified you that violations of the San Mateo Municipal Code (SMMC) exist on your 
property, and as of the date on this letter those violations have not been abated. This is your final 
notice. Failure to abate the violations may result in citations, other administrative penalties, or 
referral to the City Attorney’s Office for legal action.  
 
Immediate Life Safety & Substandard Conditions: 
1. Visible mold in both the walls and ceilings located in the bathroom and in two bedrooms, 
2. Lack of hot water reaching the minimum temperature of 110 degrees, 
3. Lack of required heat in the dwelling, 
4. Multiple electrical hazards throughout the house, (including, daisy chained extension cords, 
broken and missing outlet covers, missing light fixtures, and switches),  
5. Multiple ceiling holes causing water leaks, mold, and damage throughout the dwelling,  
6. Lack of required smoke detectors in entire dwelling, 
7. Rodents/pests in the dwelling, 
8. Termite damage, 
9. Inadequate light and ventilation, 
10. Possible gas leaking from kitchen appliance. 
 
Other Violations: 
1. Possible unpermitted construction without permits based on City observations as well as your 
attorney’s email stating active demolition of the bathroom, kitchen, drywall, and other areas 
is occurring.   
2. The bathroom shower and bathtub are not properly tiled, sealed, or waterproofed to prevent 
water intrusion, 
3. Deteriorated front door and framing, 
4. Missing weather stripping in the front door, 
5. Nonoperating sliding glass door, 
6. Deteriorated windows throughout the dwelling, 
7. Removal of an interior wall in the living room, 
8. Low hot water flow in the kitchen,

Required Corrections and Compliance Date:

addition to identifying cause of the moisture. The City has yet to receive a copy of any reports related 
to mold. Please provide a copy of the report as soon as possible.

hazards and recommendations to repair. 
5. Hire a certified Pest inspector to address the rodents and termites. Provide a report of their 
findings and recommendations to abate.  
6. Apply for and submit a building application, plans, and other necessary documents to obtain 
permits to legalize, alter, or remove the unpermitted construction and repairs to address the 
above violations.

Applicable Code Section:  
SMMC 7.14.010 PROPERTY MAINTENANCE CODE Adoption 
This chapter shall be known and may be cited as the "Property Maintenance Code" and will be 
referred to in this chapter as "this code." 
(a) The purpose of this chapter is to protect the public health, safety, and welfare in both existing residential 
and nonresidential buildings, structures, and premises within the City. 
(b) The 2021 edition of the International Property Maintenance Code as published by the International Code 
Council is adopted with amendments as listed below as the rules, regulations, and standards as to all matters 
contained therein. 
(c) A copy of this code shall be maintained on file in the office of the City Clerk.

officer, as defined in Section 829.5 of the Penal Code, excluding the presence of mold that is minor 
and found on surfaces that can accumulate moisture as part of their properly functioning and 
intended use. (11) Dampness of habitable rooms.

Every habitable space in a dwelling shall contain not less than two separate and remote receptacle outlets.

fault circuit interrupter. Every bathroom shall contain not less than one receptacle. Any new bathroom 
receptacle outlet shall have ground fault circuit interrupter protection. All receptacle outlets shall have the 
appropriate faceplate cover for the location.

SMMC 27.66.050 MAINTENANCE. (a) Routine Maintenance. Nothing in this chapter shall be construed to 
prevent routine building maintenance and repair which does not involve a change in design, material or 
appearance and is consistent with the standards and guidelines in Section 27.66.040. 
(b) The owner, lessee or other person legally in possession of a building shall comply with all applicable 
codes, laws and regulations governing the maintenance of property. It is the intent of this section to preserve 
from deliberate or inadvertent neglect the exterior features of such buildings, and of the interior portions of 
such buildings which are necessary to prevent deterioration and decay of the exterior. 
 
SMMC 7.14 PROPERTY MAINTENANCE CODE (IPMC 304) AND CALIFORNIA HEALTH AND SAFETY CODE 
17920.3 (14) General dilapidation or improper maintenance. The exterior of a structure shall be

health, safety or welfare. (IPMC 304.1.1) Unsafe conditions: (8) Roofing or roofing components that 
have defects that admit rain, roof surfaces with inadequate drainage, or any portion of the roof 
framing that is not in good repair with signs of deterioration, fatigue or without proper anchored or 
are incapable of supporting all nominal loads and resisting all load effects.

stripping, thresholds and hardware shall be maintained in good condition. Locks at all entrances to dwelling 
units and sleeping units shall tightly secure the door. (h) Section 304.16 Doors shall be tight fitting and 
ventilation openings shall be properly screened with corrosion-resistant wire mesh having openings not 
exceeding 1/4 inch in any dimension or alternate approved materials pursuant to the adopted California 
Building Standards Code.

PROPERTY OWNER AMENDED APPEAL

To Chistina Horrisberger, Director of Community Development Department
OWNER: Trina Pierce
TENANTS: Herminia Panameno, Josue N. Panameno, Patricia Panameno, and Marta Zavala

SUBJECT PREMISES: 100 N. Humboldt, San Mateo (the “Property’’)

INTRODUCTION

OWNER hereby submits this Amended Appeal of the City of San Mateo Code Enforcement’s
(CE) assessment of relocation costs — as amended (the “Assessment”).

This was a “shoot first, ask questions later” assessment. Contrary to San Mateo Municipal Code
section 7.50.030, Code Enforcement (“CE”) issued the Assessment against OWNER without
ascertaining who was responsible for conditions at the Property. The overwhelming evidence
shows that TENANTS had full control over the Property and destroyed this cherished home of
OWNER’s beloved mother.

In retaliation for OWNER serving TENANTS with a Notice to Vacate (“Notice”), because they
destroyed the Property, TENANTS sought out CE and demanded relocation costs for conditions
they caused. TENANTS weaponized CE and used CE to game the system. CE’s Assessment
without any regard to TENANTS’ misconduct sends a message that tenants who rent in San
Mateo have no obligations to maintain property and their malicious retaliatory conduct will be
rewarded.

CE assessed relocation costs prior to obtaining so much as one iota of information from the
OWNER as to liability. Moreover, once OWNER established TENANTS’ liability with a
mountain of evidence in an Appeal, CE still refused to withdraw the Assessment and proceeded
to dole out $12,736 to the TENANTS. Now, after months of requesting any evidence to support
TENANTS’ innocence, we received one email, created long after they left the Property,
containing a mixed mash of self-serving allegations, with zero support.

OWNER’s extensive evidence clearly establishes TENANTS disregarded the lease terms,
destroyed the Property warranting the Notice to Vacate and confirming that TENANTS pursuit
of relocation costs was retaliatory. CE improperly issued the Assessment. TENANTS are not
entitled to relocation costs. OWNER’s Appeal should be granted.

reaMAY iG 5elex

1

877 of 1058


--- page 878 ---
IMPROPER ASSESSMENT PROCEDURES

The Assessment is the result of a “biased and discriminatory” process. CE’s recently written
report (dated April 19, 2023) shows CE committed a major error by completely ignoring one of
the two requirements for assessing relocation costs. Per San Mateo Municipal Code section
7.50.030 for re-location costs, CE must establish two elements:

(1) The existence of conditions rendering a premises uninhabitable, and
(2) Liability for the substandard conditions.

CE failed to undertake any determination of liability prior to issuing an assessment of relocation
costs. In fact, 13 days elapsed between the date of CE’s inspection on January 13 and its
issuance of its first assessment on January 26. During those 13 days, CE never once reached
out to the OWNER to get her position. Incredulously, even after the OWNER submitted
voluminous documentation to CE clearly establishing TENANTS?’ liability for the substandard
conditions at the Property, CE refused to withdraw the Assessment. CE continues to fail to
consider OWNER’s overwhelming evidence of TENANTS?’ liability. Its unfounded Assessment
has forced the OWNER to file an Appeal, an Amended Appeal, and pay $519 to do so. As
TENANTS are liable for the uninhabitable conditions at the Property, per San Mateo Municipal
Code sections 7.50.030(b)(2) and (3), they are ineligible to receive relocation costs from
OWNER.

There should have never been an assessment from which to appeal, but OWNER has now had to
file an Appeal and Amended Appeal in order to preserve her rights. The City should summarily
grant this Appeal, immediately withdraw the Assessment and refund the appeal fee.

The Property is the cherished home of the OWNER’s mother. She leased it in a good and
habitable condition to TENANTS. TENANTS had sole possession and control of the Premises,
during which time they repeatedly breached the Lease causing extensive damages. As a result of
TENANTS’ misconduct, in November, 2022, the OWNER exercised her lawful right to evict
TENANTS with a 60-Day Notice. As the 60-Day deadline approached, TENANTS requested to
stay in the Premises. When OWNER refused, TENANTS turned to CE to exploit the process
and the OWNER and to retaliate against her. They went into overdrive in their destruction of the
Property, rendered it uninhabitable, then blamed OWNER and used the City to seek relocation
costs.

This is a case of TENANTS gaming the system to extract $12,736 in relocation costs and exploit
a senior in the process. TENANTS are ineligible for relocation costs because they are liable for
rendering the Premises uninhabitable and concealed conditions from the OWNER. They must
not benefit from their malicious deeds.

CE furthered TENANTS’ exploitation of OWNER by completely disregarding the determination
of liability before issuing the Assessment. OWNER’s evidence is overwhelming that
TENANTS are liable for the condition of the Property. As set forth in detail below, TENANTS
are not entitled to relocation costs and OWNER’s appeal should be granted.

878 of 1058


--- page 879 ---
TENANTS ARE INELIGIBLE FOR RELOCATION COSTS UNDER THE LAW

The TENANTS are ineligible for relocation costs from the OWNER based upon: (a) the San
Mateo Municipal Code (the “Code”), (b) California law, and (c) the Lease.

The three exceptions to relocation costs under the Code that apply to this matter are as follows:

(1) The TENANTS caused the damages that rendered the Premises inhabitable;

(2) The TENANTS prevented the OWNER from undertaking maintenance of the Premises
and as proven herein they not only failed to notify the OWNER of any such conditions and
provide her the opportunity to cure them, they concealed conditions from the OWNER; and
(3) There were natural disaster events that contributed to some of the conditions.

For reference, the relevant parts of San Mateo Municipal Code (the “Code” section 7.50.030 are
provided below:

(a) A tenant household shall be eligible for relocation payments from a property owner
under this chapter if the tenant household is displaced from its dwelling or room due to
the City's code enforcement activities.

(b) Notwithstanding subsection (a) above, a tenant household shall not be deemed
displaced due to code enforcement activities in any of the following cases:

2. The property owner demonstrates to the satisfaction of the Director that the
noncomplying condition was created by the tenant household or the tenant household's
guests or invitees, and was not created by the property owner or the property owner's
agent, or that the condition giving rise to the code enforcement activities existed at the
time that the tenant household occupied the dwelling or room and that the tenant
household occupied the dwelling or room for the purpose of receiving relocation benefits;

3. The property owner demonstrates to the satisfaction of the Director that the tenant
household unreasonably prevented the property owner or the property owner's agent from
undertaking maintenance or repairs that would have prevented or rectified the
noncomplying condition;

7. The tenant household is required to vacate the dwelling or room due solely to damage
resulting from an earthquake, fire, flood, natural disaster, civil disturbance, or accident
outside the control of the property owner, if (a) the vacation is required within six months

879 of 1058


--- page 880 ---
of such event, and (b) the property owner demonstrates to the satisfaction of the Director
that such damage was not caused by the acts or the negligence of the property owner or
by a preexisting condition in the building in violation of applicable building, housing,
fire, or other health and safety codes. (Emphasis Added).

State Law provides that a tenant has an affirmative duty to keep a premises habitable and a
landlord is not liable for damages caused by the tenant. (California Civil Code section 1941.2)
California law also provides that if there is a substandard condition, a tenant must notify the
landlord and allow the landlord a reasonable time to repair the condition (California Civil Code

section 1942).

The Lease specifically requires the TENANTS to report a substandard condition to the OWNER
and allow a reasonable time to repair it. If TENANTS cause damage to the Premises, OWNER
has the right to terminate the Lease and TENANTS will be held responsible for losses, damages,
and repair costs.

As set forth below, the OWNER will discuss this legal authority in the context of the alleged
conditions on the Premises.

BACKGROUND FACTS

THE HOME & THE LEASE: 100 N. Humboldt was built in 1940, in the redline district of San
Mateo. The OWNER’s family bought the home in the 1950’s because it was the only area of San
Mateo in which her family could buy a home. The OWNER and her siblings grew up in this
home. It is a cherished home and is the bedrock of their generational wealth.

The OWNER leased (the “Lease”) and turned over possession of her family’s home to
TENANTS, in a condition that was clean, sanitary, in good repair, and completely free of any
infestations. (See Exhibits A-C and D.) In fact at that time of the Lease, the Premises passed
inspection to qualify as Section 8 housing. In short, there was no question that the Premises
were habitable. (See Exhibit D.)

Upon Lease execution through to January 31, 2023, TENANTS had the exclusive possession
and control of the Premises. Landlord believed that when the tenancy ended the TENANTS
would return the Premises in the same condition as existed upon their move-in, except for normal

wear and tear.

Under the terms of the Lease and California Law, TENANTS were obligated to:

e Keep the unit in a clean and habitable condition.

880 of 1058


--- page 881 ---
e Keep fixtures clean and sanitary.
e Use the rental unit for living, sleeping, cooking, or dining purposes only.

60-DAY NOTICE TO VACATE: During the tenancy, TENANTS failed on multiple levels to
maintain the Premises. As a result, on November 17, 2022, the OWNER served TENANTS with
a 60-Day Notice to Vacate for the following breaches of the Lease:

L. No Pets —- TENANTS kept 4 dogs and chickens on the Premises. No permission
was ever asked for or given.

Zs Damages caused by occupants entering the Premises through a window which
Landlord told TENANTS multiple times not to do, and caused the Landlord to replace
the window three times.

ee TENANTS secretly operating a business at the Premises, advertised by someone
the Landlord does not know.

4. TENANTS altering the Premises - More and more walls going up, without
permits or permission from the Landlord.

5. Continuing to have people moving in and out of the premises without the
Landlord's knowledge or permission.

6. Fire risks, continually placing things in front of a heater, which the OWNER told
TENANTS not to do.

ee Overflowing garbage and trash bins, uncovered, and bags of trash by the bins — a
health issue which can cause rodent problems. Trash and beer cans visible from the front
yard also needed to be moved out of sight to the backyard. (See Ex. E.)

As the 60-Day deadline approached, the TENANTS tried to pay the OWNER rent to continue to
live at the Premises and requested that they be allowed to stay another two months. The
OWNER refused to accept the rent or allow the TENANTS to stay longer. She wanted them to
vacate because of their repeated breaches of the Lease causing extensive damage. She advised
the TENANTS that she was upset that they continued to not care or even try to address the issues
of people climbing out windows requiring her to replace the window three times, their

THE TENANTS ARE LIABLE FOR THE SUBSTANDARD CONDITIONS

1. TENANTS Caused Mold at the Premises by Failing to Keep it Clean and Concealed

these Conditions from OWNER

Under Municipal Code section 7.50.030(b)(2), OWNER is not liable for re-location costs due to
substandard conditions caused by TENANTS. State Law also provides that a tenant has an
affirmative duty to keep a premises habitable and a landlord is not liable for damages caused by
the tenant. (California Civil Code section 1941.2)

TENANTS caused mold by failing to clean, excessive dirt, putting up and taking down walls,
ripping off cabinet doors, punching holes in walls and doors, living in squalor of their own
making. (See Exhibits A-C and I, before and after photos.) TENANTS’ bedrooms contained
half eaten food TENANTS prepared food there. As set forth above, the TENANTS admitted via
text that they failed to maintain the Premises. (Ex. F: 1-1-23 Text.) Accordingly, OWNER is not
liable for mold and it is absurd that CE would try to hold OWNER liable for these tenant-caused

conditions.

Moreover, per Muni Code section 7.50.030(b)(3), California Civil Code Section 1942 and the
Lease, OWNER is not liable for concealed conditions. TENANTS purposefully concealed these
conditions by keeping windows covered and all doors closed off from the OWNER when she
was on site and intimidated her into staying in the specific area she was there to address. Tenant,
Josue N. Panameno, frequently intimidated the OWNER. (Given the multiple police reports
referenced above, the OWNER was justified in her fear of the TENANTS). (Ex. J.) The
TENANTS made it impossible for the OWNER to know this condition or to be able to abate it.

It is also noted that the OWNER did not list any mold in her November 2022, Notice to Vacate
because it was concealed from her so she was unaware of it. (See Ex. E.)

The OWNER has clearly demonstrated the TENANTS not only caused the mold at the Premises,
but that they prevented the OWNER from repairing the condition by failing to give her notice
and that they actually concealed the condition. As such, per Code sections 7.50.030 (b)(2) and
(b)(3), TENANTS are NOT entitled to relocation costs for this condition.

885 of 1058


--- page 886 ---
2. There Was No Hot Water Issue, Nor did the TENANTS ever inform the OWNER of

Such an Issue

There is no factual basis for this clam. TENANTS admit OWNER put in a new water heater in
May, 2022. Per the Lease and an established course of conduct, the TENANTS notified the
OWNER that the water heater needed repair. The OWNER installed one promptly (Exhibit G
reflects Landlord’s Repairs during the tenancy.) At no time thereafter did the TENANTS
notify the OWNER that water temperature was an issue and there is no evidence of any
such claim. TENANTS’ purported claim to CE about water after OWNER asked them to vacate
the Property is just not credible. Moreover, the OWNER’s plumber actually confirmed the hot
water heater was appropriately set for between 110 and 120 degrees.

3. TENANTS Never Notified the OWNER about a Lack of Heat

There is no factual basis for this clam. TENANTS failed to notify the OWNER of any heating
issues during their tenancy and have provided no evidence of any such notice. They raised this
apparent issue after the OWNER served them with a 60-Day Notice to Vacate. The OWNER
had no way of knowing about any supposed heat issue, should one exist. TENANTS had full
possession and control of the Premises. TENANTS were responsible for the heat and the PG&E
bill was in their name.

Per the Lease and California Civil Code section 1942, without prior notice of this alleged
condition, the OWNER cannot be held responsible for it. Per Muni Code 7.50.030(b)(3),
concealment relieves OWNER from liability. OWNER therefore has no liability for relocation
costs.

4. TENANTS Created and Maintained the Electrical Hazards

TENANTS created and maintained electrical hazards. They did so even after the OWNER spent
$3000 upgrading and relocating the electrical panel and installing new plugs in each of the
rooms. (See Ex. G.) Whenever the OWNER saw these conditions, she asked the TENANTS to
remove them. (See Exs. I & E.) Despite the OWNER’s requests, the TENANTS continued to
maintain these hazardous electrical conditions. Under the Muni Code 7.50.030(b)(2) TENANTS
caused the condition, violated the Civil Code section 1941.2 (duty to maintain), and as such they
are not entitled to relocation costs.

Moreover, the TENANTS concealed other locations of these conditions and their damages to
electrical outlets, holes in walls by closing doors and intimidating her to stay in a confined space
when on the Premises. This intimidation was well-founded given that TENANTS were violent
and likely possessed gun ammunition. As TENANTS purposefully failed to notify the OWNER
of the alleged conditions or provide her an opportunity to cure them, per Muni Code
7.50.030(b)(3), Civil Code section 1942, and the Lease, OWNER is not liable.

886 of 1058

5. The OWNER is Not Liable For Water Leaking In

Roof: Upon notice from the TENANTS, the OWNER addressed roof issues to prevent leaking.
Following the recent multiple atmospheric rivers that hit San Mateo, the roof leaked again and on
January 9, 2023, days before TENANTS were to vacate the Premises, the TENANTS notified
the OWNER via text that the roof was leaking. The OWNER took immediate steps to mitigate
the leak. (As for TENANTS?’ claims about the kitchen roof collapsing and their video, it appears
staged. It is not credible that it fell at the exact time they were filming.)

It is important to note that this condition did not make the Premises uninhabitable. Moreover,
OWNER acted in a prompt and responsible manner to rectify this situation caused by a natural
disaster. As such, relocation costs are not appropriate per Muni Code section 7.50.030(b)(7).

Ceiling and Wall Holes: On January 10, 2023, in response to the notice of the roof leak, the
OWNER found that the TENANTS, without authorization, in breach of the Lease, and the City’s
Building Code, had once again erected walls in the living room and dining room. (See photos,
Ex. I - before and after.) The OWNER included this breach of the Lease in her Notice to Vacate
but the TENANTS just kept blatantly disregarding her requests to not do this. (See Exhibits E &
I.) Then, before CE’s January 13, 3023, inspection, the TENANTS removed these illegal walls,
leaving terrible holes in the walls and ceilings. (See Ex. I - photos). OWNER’s evidence clearly
shows TENANTS caused these conditions (and any resulting leak or mold). Moreover, OWNER
had no prior notice of them or an opportunity to cure as per the Lease and California law. Per
Code sections 7.50.030(b)(2) and (b)(3), the TENANTS are NOT entitled to relocation costs for
these alleged conditions.

6. TENANTS Removed the Working Smoke Detectors

TENANTS removed the smoke detectors and put them back up multiple times. OWNER is not
liable for the condition caused by TENANTS. (S.M Muni Code §7.50.030(b)(2).) TENANTS
had possession and an obligation to maintain property, including smoke detectors. (Civ. Code §
1941.2)

The OWNER has clearly established that when TENANTS took possession of the Premises they
acknowledged that working smoke detectors were present and agreed to keep them functional
with regular battery replacement. (See Exhibits A-C.) The Lease also mandated that the
TENANTS inform the OWNER immediately, in writing, of any defect, malfunction or failure of
such detectors. There is no evidence that TENANT ever notified OWNER of any problems with
the smoke detectors.

Per the Lease and California law, the OWNER cannot be held responsible for the conditions the
TENANTS caused or those for which she had no notice and an opportunity to cure them. As

such, per Code sections 7.50.030(b)(2) and (b)(3), the TENANTS are NOT entitled to relocation

living in squalor, attracting rodents and pests. Under the Lease, TENANTS are responsible for
preventing this condition. The OWNER’s Notice to Vacate, included TENANTS’ perpetually

incredible that CE blatantly refused to acknowledge the TENANTS’ actions in this regard. (See

As there is no question the TENANTS caused the infestations, the OWNER cannot be held liable
for this condition. Per Code section 7.50.030(b)(2) and Civil Code section 1941.2, the
TENANTS are NOT entitled to relocation costs for this alleged condition.

8. OWNER Had No Notice or Reason to Know The Home Had Termite Damage;

The OWNER turned over possession of her family’s home to the TENANTS free of infestations.
(See Exhibits A-C, paragraph 11). The TENANTS never notified the OWNER about termites or
provided her with an opportunity to cure these purported conditions. Per the Lease and Civil
Code section 1942, without prior notice of these alleged conditions and an opportunity to cure
them, the OWNER cannot be held responsible for them. Moreover, per Muni Code section
7.50.030(b)(3), OWNER is not responsible for concealed conditions.

9. The TENANTS Restricted Lighting and Ventilation

The TENANTS’ makeshift attempts to subdivide the rooms interfered with ventilation and
lighting. (See Ex. I.) The OWNER’s Notice to Vacate included TENANTS’ breach of the Lease
by subdividing. Again, TENANTS kept blatantly disregarding her requests to not do this
dividing. (See Exhibits E & I.)

The OWNER has clearly demonstrated she provided the Property to TENANTS with all lighting
fixtures operational and that any inadequate light or ventilation in the Premises is attributed to
the TENANTS and per Code sections 7.50.030(b)(2) and (b)(3), the TENANTS are NOT entitled
to relocation costs for these alleged conditions.

OTHER DAMAGES

CONCLUSION

The City’s assessment of relocation costs without so much as one call or any information from
OWNER concerning liability was in violation of the San Mateo Municipal Code, which clearly
requires undertaking a determination of liability prior to any assessment.

When OWNER provided substantial evidence clearly showing TENANTS destroyed OWNER’s
generational family home, CE ignored it and then spent months trying to get evidence from the
TENANTS to somehow show they were not liable for destroying the Property. Said “evidence”
is woefully deficient and unsubstantiated.

Per San Mateo Municipal Code sections 7.50.030(b)(2) and (b)(3), and the overwhelming weight
of the evidence showing that the TENANTS caused the damages and failed to notify the
OWNER or provide her an opportunity to cure any of the claimed conditions, the relocation
assessment is wholly inappropriate. OWNER respectfully requests that the City Council

Tenants failed to notify Landlord and allow Landlord an opportunity to cure the alleged
substandard conditions in the City’s Notice. The Lease mandates that Tenants immediately
notify Landlord of needed repairs and provide Landlord an opportunity to cure the conditions.
In fact, Tenants had always followed this notice procedure throughout their tenancy and Landlord
provided the needed repairs. (Exhibit G: Landlord’s Repairs) It is only now after Tenants
received a Notice to Vacate that Tenants are claiming uninhabitable conditions to the City,
conditions which as explained below they created and concealed from Landlord.

The Lease expressly provides that Tenants shall “immediately notify Landlord of any defects or
dangerous conditions in and about the Premises of which they become aware” and if Tenants or
their guests cause the damages they shall “reimburse Landlord, ... for the cost of any repairs to
the premises, ... damaged by Tenants or their guest or invitees through misuse or neglect.” (See
Exs. A-C, Rental Agreements, paragraph 11 sections (2) and (3).)

Throughout the tenancy and prior to the Landlord’s Notice to Vacate, Tenants would notify
Landlord, in writing via text messages, of any needed repairs to the Premises and Landlord would
make the repairs. Landlord has extensive records documenting repairs made and replacing
fixtures, including windows, a water heater, and electrical panel. (Ex. G: Landlord’s Repairs)

On January 1, 2023, following extraordinary rains from multiple atmospheric rivers, Tenants
notified Landlord that the roof was leaking and water had entered the Premises. Landlord
immediately took actions to mitigate water coming in and began contracting with a roofer for a
permanent repair. (Exhibit H: Landlord’s Contract for Roof Replacement.) Tenants also made
a vague reference to a plumbing issue on January 1. Landlord retained a plumber to inspect and
repair the item. It will be repaired within the week of January 30th.

Aside from the recent leaking roof and plumbing issue, Tenants did not notify Landlord about
other damages or needed repairs as identified in the City’s Notice, nor did they provide Landlord

 Landlord’s Notice to Vacate gave Tenants 60 days to vacate. Had Landlord known she could have served a three-
day notice to vacate for breach of the Lease she would have done so. See California Code of Civil Procedure, section
1161(4), which provides in relevant part as follows: any tenant, assigning or subletting or committing waste upon the
premises, contrary to the conditions of the lease, or maintaining, committing, or permitting the maintenance or
commission of a nuisance upon the premises or using the premises for an unlawful purpose thereby terminates the
lease, and the Landlord is entitled to restitution of possession of the premises.

with an opportunity to cure. Moreover, as set forth below Tenants had exclusive possession and
control over the Premises, during which time they caused extensive damages.’ Tenants
committed waste upon the Premises while also failing to clean and maintain the Premises causing
a nuisance, deterioration, and infestations.

Ii. TENANTS COMMITTED WASTE ON THE PROPERTY AND SHOULD NOT BENEFIT
FROM THEIR DESTRUCTION OF LANDLORD’S FAMILY HOME

This is not a case of a landlord renting a substandard unit. Quite the contrary, Landlord rented
her family home in a habitable condition. (See Exhibit D photos). Tenants who had exclusive
control over the Premises repeatedly breached the Lease causing waste and creating dangerous
conditions. After receiving a Notice to Vacate, Tenants caused further damages to the Property
and then complained to Code Enforcement in an effort to exploit the system. They should not
be able to profit from their misconduct and destruction of Landlord’s family home.

Tenants signed the February 2017 rental agreement and amended agreements in June 2018 and
January 2019, agreeing that the Premises at 100 N. Humboldt Street was clean, sanitary, in good
repair, free of infestations of rodents, cockroaches and other insects and pests, and included
working smoke detectors. (See Exhibits A-C, paragraphs 11 and 20 and Exhibit D photos.)

Since taking possession of the Premise Tenants repeatedly breached the Lease by committing
waste, altering the structure, failing to clean and maintain the Premises causing a nuisance,
deterioration, and infestations. Exhibit I hereto contains photos of the damages caused by shows
Tenants misconduct and destruction of the Premise including the following:

November 17, 2022

To: All the Tenants Residing at 100 N. Humboldt St
This notice serves as your 60 day notice to vacate the property at 100 N. Humboldt St.

The notice is pertaining to all the people listed on the Lease Agreement and all those living in
the home, who are not listed on the Lease Agreement.

Attached with this notice is a copy of the AB1482, which covers legal protection of both the
Landlord and Renter’s rights. You are being evicted for a breach of material terms of the Lease.
You will see by law you are not protected by the Tenant Protection Act (AB1482).

Due to the damage that has been caused to the property, all individuals must vacate by
January 17, 2023. Due to the various damages caused to the interior and exterior of the
property it will require major repairs and renovations.

Because of the many Lease Violation extreme damage has been thrust_upon the property at
100 N. Humboldt St

Violations:

1) Lease Agreement states NO Pets. Yet, you have 4 dogs living on the property. Also,
Chickens, now there are 4 baby chicks. No permission was given or even asked.

2) Multiple times you have been told not to enter and exit thru the window. This action has
caused damage and | have had to replace the window 3 times. Yet you still continue to
disregard my request.

3) The property is for residential use only. Yet, you have allowed an advertising by Mendez to
use the address of 100 N. Humboldt St, San Mateo as your business. No one asked could a
business be run out of my rental home. Which would be a violation and a fine charged to

me. | do not even know this person This Violation Must Stop Iimmediatedly. The post will
need to be removed from Next Door and any other Advertisement.

4) More and more walls are going up altering the home, which continues without my
permission. This again is a violation and | can be fined.
5) You continue to have people move into the residence without my knowledge or my

permission
6) Continually you have been asked not place anything in front of the heater. Whether the
heater is on or off, due to a fire risk and a fire violation.

NOTICE LANGUAGE REQUIREMENTS IN THE TENANT PROTECTION ACT OF 2019
(AB 1482)

1. REQUIRED NOTICE LANGUAGE for tenancies in units that are EXEMPT from the Tenant
Protection Act because the property meets the requirements detailed in Civil Code §§
1947.12(d)(5) and 1946.2(e)(8). Specifically, this would be a “residential real property that
is alienable separate from the title to any other dwelling unit” with no corporate
ownership. E.g. single-family home on its own parcel, condominium.

The paragraph below should be included in any lease entered into after July 1, 2020. For
existing tenancies, a notice with this paragraph should be provided to the tenant.

“This property is not subject to the rent limits imposed by Section 1947.12 of the Civil
Code and is not subject to the just cause requirements of Section 1946.2 of the Civil
Code. This property meets the requirements of Sections 1947.12 (d)(5) and 1946.2
(e)(8) of the Civil Code and the owner is not any of the following: (1) a real estate
investment trust, as defined by Section 856 of the Internal Revenue Code; (2) a
corporation; or (3) a limited liability company in which at least one member is a
corporation.”

2. REQUIRED NOTICE LANGUAGE for tenancies in units that are NOT EXEMPT from the
Tenant Protection Act.

- For tenancies existing prior to July 1, 2020, a notice with the language below must be
given to the tenant no later than August 1, 2020, or as an addendum to the lease or
rental agreement.

- For tenancies beginning or being renewed on or after July 1, 2020, language below
must be included as an addendum to the lease or rental agreement, or as a written
notice signed by the tenant, with a copy provided to the tenant.

- The notice or lease provision shall be in no less than 12-point type, in the language
the original contract was negotiated in, and shall include the following:

“California law limits the amount your rent can be increased. See Section 1947.12 of
the Civil Code for more information. California law also provides that after all of the
tenants have continuously and lawfully occupied the property for 12 months or more
or at least one of the tenants has continuously and lawfully occupied the property for
24 months or more, a landlord must provide a statement of cause in any notice to
terminate a tenancy. See Section 1946.2 of the Civil Code for more information.”

*This flyer is for informational use only*

representation. For legal services, please contact an attorney or a lawyer referral service.

Subject: Trina Pierce 
  
  
 
Hello SMCcm, it is with great concern that I once again must contact you. I my last letter lacked 
understanding on a few areas. 
Concerning the placing of the tenants refrigerators, they were supplied for myself, Mr. Larry who was 
there when I moved in, and a couple that moved in after I did., 
Mr.Larry had been there for 9 yrs.. Mrs.Taylor (Trina’s mother)had allowed him to use the kitchen fridge 
and I didn’t want to inconvenience him.Ms. Pierce put in 2other refrigerators that were located in the back 
area near the washroom (as you recall I stated we also had a washer and dryer). No one was allowed 
any type of appliances in their sleeping area’s. 
Secondly Ms.Pierce had nothing to do with the upstairs heating unit being turned off. During an inspection 
my worker (from Housing Authority) decided it would be more prudent to have it disconnected. That was 
only 1 of the 3heating units in the house. The unit directly below my bedroom was more than enough to 
heat the back are of the house, then there was another unit in the front of the house. 
As I stated before if there had been any type of problems with the house I would never have been 
approved to stay there and housing in San Mateo county is not a pushover. 
I’m sure you didn’t intend to twist my truths, I just felt it was necessary to make things clear and honest. 
I thank you for your time and please see my words as I’ve stated them please do not add or take anything 
away. 
Valorie Rivers
